Tahayu on Income from Two Slaves: Sahibayn vs. Abu Hanifa
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tahayu on two slaves' earnings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on tahayu on the earnings of two jointly-owned slaves and explain the qiyas reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
Tahayu on two slaves' earnings splits the Hanafi school: Sahibayn permit by analogy; Abu Hanifa forbids due to greater disparity.

This passage examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of temporal division (tahayu) of the earnings from two jointly-owned slaves. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize it to tahayu on usufructs, while Imam Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy, citing greater disparity between distinct slaves and the absence of necessity. Understanding this reasoning deepens your grasp of how qiyas and necessity interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positions
State clearly what the Sahibayn permit and what Abu Hanifa forbids regarding tahayu on the income of two slaves.
The Sahibayn permit; Abu Hanifa forbids.
2
Analyze Sahibayn's qiyas
The Sahibayn draw an analogy (qiyas) to tahayu on usufructs (manafi), which is allowed. Identify the 'illa (effective cause): the need to partition a joint benefit that cannot be physically divided.
They equate the earnings (ghallah) to usufruct for the purpose of tahayu.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's objection
Abu Hanifa argues that the disparity between two different slaves is greater than the temporal disparity in one slave, so the ruling should be even stricter. Also, income can be physically divided (as ayn), so no necessity exists.
He distinguishes between khidmah (service) – where necessity justifies tahayu – and ghallah (income).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If tahayu is allowed, each partner takes one slave for a period and keeps all earnings. If not, they must hire out the slaves jointly and divide the proceeds.
Practical consequence for joint ownership.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text does not explicitly give a mufta bihi, but notes that only the Sahibayn permit. Typically, the position of the Sahibayn is more expansive and often relied upon in later Hanafi works.
Consider the authority weight: this is a recognized ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text

وكذا يجوز فى العبدين عندهما اعتبارا بالتهايؤ فى المنافع ولا يجوز عنده لان التفاوت في اعيان الرقيق اكثر منه من حيث الزمان فى العبد الواحد فاولى ان يمتنع الجواز التهايؤ فى الخدمة جوز ضرورة ولا ضرورة فى الغلة لإمكان قسمتها لكونها عينا ولان الظاهر هو التسامح في الخدمة والاستقصاء في الاستغلال فلا يتقاسان. ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی تہائیاً جائز ہے دو غلاموں میں صاحبین کے نزدیک منافع میں تنہا یو پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ تفاوت اعیان رقیق میں زیادہ ہے ان تفاوت سے زمان کی حیثیت سے عبد واحد کے اندر تو بدرجہ اولیٰ یہ بات ہوگی کہ جواز ممتنع ہو اور خدمت کے اندر تبا یو بر بناء ضرورت جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے اور کرایہ پر دینے میں کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے غلہ کی قسمت سے ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے غلہ کے عین ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اس لئے کہ ظاہر وہ تسامح (دلیری) ہے خدمت میں اور بخل ہے کرایہ پر دینے میں تو یہ ایک دوسرے پر قیاس نہ ہوں گے۔ تشریح دو غلام ہیں جن کو دونوں شریک استغلال کے لئے ایک ایک کو لیں تو یہ طریقہ صرف صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے انہوں نے استقلال کو تبایو فی المنافع پر قیاس کیا ہے۔ اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ مہایات جائز نہیں کیونکہ ایک غلام میں مہایات ہو یکے بعد دیگرے استغلال کے لئے تو وہی طریقہ جائز نہیں کیونکہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ وہ ایک مہینہ میں اتنا کما دے کہ دوسرے مہینے میں اتنا نہ کما سکے تو اس تفاوت کی وجہ سے جب عبد واحد میں مہایات جائز نہیں تو عبدین میں بدرجہ اولی جائز نہ ہوگی کیونکہ یہاں تفاوت اور زیادہ ہے کیونکہ یہاں اعیان جدا جدا ہیں جن میں جلی ہوتا ظاہر ہے۔ مصنف اسی مفہوم کو لان التفاوت فی اعیان الرفیق الخ سے بیان کیا ہے۔ سوال ... آپ نے مہایات فی المنافع کو عبد واحد اور عبدین دونوں میں جائز قرار دیا ہے؟ جواب وہاں ضرورت ہے اور غلہ میں کوئی ضرورت نہیں کیو نکہ کہ منافع نہیں بلکہ مین واحہ پر ہے جس کی خود تقسیم کی جاسکتی ہے کہ وہ دنوں مشترک طور پران کو کرایہ پر دیں اور جو آمدنی ہو اسکو تقسیم کر لیں نیز خدمت کے اندر تفاوت سے دی چشم پوشی سے کام لیتا ہے
And similarly, it is permissible in two slaves according to them (the two companions), based on analogy with tahayu on usufructs, but not permissible according to him (Abu Hanifa) because the disparity in the entities of slaves is greater than the disparity in time in a single slave, so it is even more appropriate that permissibility is prevented. Tahayu on service (khidmah) is allowed out of necessity, but there is no necessity in rent (ghallah) because it is possible to divide it as it is a physical asset (ayn), and because apparent is lenience in service and strictness in exploitation, so they are not analogous. Translation: And similarly, tahayu is permissible in two slaves according to the Sahibayn, by analogy to tahayu on usufructs, but not permissible according to Abu Hanifa because the disparity in the physical bodies of slaves is greater than the disparity in time within a single slave, so permissibility is even more unlikely. Tahayu on service (khidmah) is allowed due to necessity, but there is no necessity in income (ghallah) because it can be divided as it is a physical asset, and because people are generally lenient in service but strict in income, so the two cases are not comparable. Explanation: The passage discusses two slaves owned jointly. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit tahayu on their earnings by analogy to tahayu on usufructs (like renting a house). Imam Abu Hanifa forbids it because the inequality between two distinct slaves (different abilities) is greater than the inequality in one slave over time, and since tahayu on a single slave's earnings is also not permissible according to him (due to potential inequality), it is even more forbidden for two slaves. Moreover, any necessity (darurah) that allows tahayu on services does not apply to earnings, because earnings can be divided as actual property. The question and answer reinforce that tahayu on usufruct is permitted out of necessity, but earnings can be divided directly.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of tahayu (temporal division) on the earnings (istighlal) of two jointly-owned slaves. According to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), it is permissible by qiyas (analogy) to tahayu on usufruct (like renting property). However, Imam Abu Hanifa rejects this, arguing that the disparity between two distinct slaves in terms of earning capacity is greater than the disparity in one slave's earnings over time. Since tahayu on a single slave's earnings is not permissible (as it can cause inequality), it is even more so for two slaves. Additionally, tahayu on services (khidmah) is allowed out of necessity, but there is no such necessity for earnings because earnings can be divided as physical property (ayn). The question and answer clarify that in usufruct-based tahayu, necessity arises because usufruct cannot be divided physically, but earnings can. Therefore, the two cases are not analogous. The text highlights the Hanafi principle of prioritizing necessity and avoiding excessive inequality.

Key Terms
عبد (abd): Slave; here used as an income-generating asset through labor or hire.
رقيق (raqiq): Slave; plural of 'abd; here refers to the physical entities of slaves.
خدمة (khidmah): Service; the work performed by a slave.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that permits otherwise prohibited actions, such as tahayu when physical division is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Imam Abu Hanifa disallow tahayu on the income of two slaves?
A) Because slaves cannot be used for income.
B) Because the inequality between two distinct slaves is greater than temporal inequality in one slave, and there is no necessity.
C) Because Sahibayn disagreed with him.
D) Because it leads to riba.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, tahayu on income from two distinct assets is subject to ikhtilaf: Sahibayn permit by qiyas on usufruct; Abu Hanifa forbids due to greater disparity and lack of necessity.

Tahayi' of Two Houses: Time-Based vs Physical Apportionment
Explains the ruling on apportionment of two houses for rental income

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between time-based and physical tahayi' in rental property and determine when excess income is shared among co-owners.

Core Idea
In time-based tahayi', partners act as agents; in physical apportionment, each owns their portion exclusively.

In the previous lesson, we learned about tahayi' in a single house. Now, what happens when two co-owners divide two separate houses for rental income? Is the arrangement valid? And if one house earns more than the other, must the excess be shared? This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah answers these questions, drawing a critical distinction between time-sharing and physical division of properties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note that the passage first references tahayi' in a single house (time-based turns). Then it presents a new scenario: each partner takes one house permanently to rent out. Identify these two types.
Time-based: each uses the same house in alternating periods. Physical: each gets a separate house exclusively.
2
State the ruling for the new scenario
The author states that in Zahir al-Riwayah, this physical apportionment is also permissible based on the same evidence as the single-house case.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the core transmitted position of the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the difference in profit sharing
In the first scenario, any extra income earned during one's turn is shared with the partner. In the second scenario, the extra income belongs exclusively to the partner whose house earned it.
This is the key practical difference.
4
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The reason: in time-based tahayi', the partner using the house is a deputy (wakil) for the other, so profits must be returned like a loan. In physical apportionment, the houses are distinct, so each has exclusive rights to their own property's profits.
The illa (legal cause) is the nature of possession: agency vs ownership.
5
Apply the distinction to new cases
Consider a scenario where co-owners alternate houses each year vs each takes one house forever. Determine whether excess income is shared based on the type.
This builds skill in classifying real-world partnership agreements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پہلے مسئلہ میں مہایات دار واحد میں تھی جس کا حکم بیان کر چکا ہے اور اگر مہایات دو گھروں میں ہوں اس طریقہ پر کہ ایک گھر زید کوں کیا کہ وہ اس کو کرایہ پر چلائے اور دو ۔ ا نمروکہ کہ اس کو وہ کرایہ پر چلائے تو ظاہر الروایہ میں اس سابق دلیل سے یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ پہلی صورت میں اور اس میں یہ فرق ہے کہ پہلی صورت میں اگر کسی کی باری میں آمدنی زیادہ ہو تو اس میں دونوں شریک ہوں گے اور دوسری صورت میں اگر ایک طرف زیادہ آمدنی ہو تو زیادتی میں شرکت نہیں ہوگی اور ان دونوں میں فرق کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ دوسری صورت میں زیادہ ہو تو میں یہ افراز اور تمیز کے معنی رائج ہے کیونکہ تحصیل منافع کا زمانہ ایک ہے اور پہلی صورت میں وصول منفعت یکے بعد دیگرے ہے تو اس کو قرض شمار کیا جائے گا کہ یہ اپنے ساتھی کا وکیل ہے اور جب وکیل پھر اتو ساتھی کا حصہ واپس کرنا ضروری ہو گیا۔
In the first case, the tahayi' was in a single house whose ruling has been explained. If the tahayi' is in two houses in such a way that one house is given to Zaid to rent out, and the other to Amr to rent out, then in Zahir al-Riwayah, by the previous evidence, this is also permissible. In the first case and in this there is a difference: in the first case, if someone's turn brings more income, then both partners share it; in the second case, if one side brings more income, there is no partnership in the excess. The reason for the difference is that in the second case, the excess involves apportionment and distinction because the time of earning profit is one; in the first case, the receipt of benefit is successive, so it will be considered a loan, that this one is a deputy for his partner, and when the deputy receives profit, it becomes necessary to return the partner's share.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah clarifies the ruling on tahayi' (apportionment) when two partners agree to divide two houses between them for rental income, each taking one house to exploit exclusively. The author states that this is permissible according to Zahir al-Riwayah, relying on the same evidence as for a single house. However, a crucial distinction is made: if the tahayi' is based on time (e.g., each uses the same house in alternate years), any extra income earned during one's turn is shared with the partner because it is considered a loan or agency relationship. But if each takes a separate house permanently (physical apportionment), any excess income earned by one is not shared because the houses are distinctly owned. The reasoning is that in time-based tahayi', the partner is acting as an agent for the other, so profits must be returned; in physical apportionment, each has exclusive rights to their designated property.

Key Terms
مہایات (tahayi'): Apportionment or division of usufruct (manafi') among co-owners by allocating specific times or parts to each.
وکیل (wakil): Agent or deputy; in this context, the partner using the property in time-based tahayi' acts as a wakil for the other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of tahayi' of two houses for rent, if one partner's designated house earns more than the other's, is the excess shared?
A) Yes, always shared because they are partners.
B) No, never shared because each is independent.
C) Only shared if the tahayi' was time-based (each uses both houses in turns).
D) Only shared if the tahayi' was physical (each takes one house permanently).

Key Takeaway
In physical apportionment of two houses, each partner's profits are exclusive; only in time-sharing must excess be shared.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tahayi' in Two Slaves for Rental Income
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tahayi' of two slaves for rental income

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on tahayi' in two slaves for rental income, distinguishing the proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the practical consequence of the difference.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa prohibits tahayi' in two slaves for rental income; Sahibayn permit it by analogy with usufruct.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of apportioning (tahayi') two jointly owned slaves for exploitation (istighlal) by each partner taking one slave for rental income. Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits it on the grounds of greater disparity and lack of necessity, while the Sahibayn allow it by analogy with tahayi' in usufruct. Understanding this difference deepens your grasp of the Hanafi school's reasoning methodology and the role of necessity in legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and positions
Identify the legal question: Is tahayi' permissible when two partners own two slaves and each takes one for rental income? State the position of Abu Hanifa (not permissible) and the Sahibayn (permissible).
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Analyze the three grounds for prohibition: (1) a fortiori reasoning (greater disparity in bodies than in time), (2) no necessity since rent can be divided as tangible property, (3) people are lenient in service but strict in rental matters.
The a fortiori argument is based on the already-established impermissibility of tahayi' in a single slave's time.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Understand their analogy: just as tahayi' in usufruct (manafi') is permissible, so too is tahayi' in the rental income from two slaves, since the rental is a form of usufruct.
They equate 'istighlal' (exploitation/rental) with 'manafi' (usufruct) in permissibility.
4
Evaluate the response and thamarah
Note Abu Hanifa's rebuttal: the analogy fails because the disparity is greater and the attitude towards service and rental differ. Identify the practical consequence: if partners proceed, Abu Hanifa would deem the arrangement invalid, while the Sahibayn would uphold it.
The text does not give a tarjih (preference); the dispute remains unresolved in this passage.
5
Reflect on the usul implications
Consider how this dispute illustrates the use of qiyas and istihsan in Hanafi usul: Sahibayn use general analogy, while Abu Hanifa restricts it based on istihsan (considering disparity and necessity).
This is a typical intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf rooted in different evaluations of the effective cause (illah).

Source Text

الاستغلال فلا يتقاسان
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی تہائیاً جائز ہے دو غلاموں میں صاحبین کے نزدیک منافع میں تنہا یو پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ تفاوت اعیان رقیق میں زیادہ ہے ان تفاوت سے زمان کی حیثیت سے عبد واحد کے اندر تو بدرجہ اولیٰ یہ بات ہوگی کہ جواز ممتنع ہو اور خدمت کے اندر تبا یو بر بناء ضرورت جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے اور کرایہ پر دینے میں کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے غلہ کی قسمت سے ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے غلہ کے عین ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اس لئے کہ ظاہر وہ تسامح (دلیری) ہے خدمت میں اور بخل ہے کرایہ پر دینے میں تو یہ ایک دوسرے پر قیاس نہ ہوں گے۔ تشریح دو غلام ہیں جن کو دونوں شریک استغلال کے لئے ایک ایک کو لیں تو یہ طریقہ صرف صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے انہوں نے استقلال کو تبایو فی المنافع پر قیاس کیا ہے۔
اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ مہایات جائز نہیں کیونکہ ایک غلام میں مہایات ہو یکے بعد دیگرے استغلال کے لئے تو وہی طریقہ جائز نہیں کیونکہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ وہ ایک مہینہ میں اتنا کما دے کہ دوسرے مہینے میں اتنا نہ کما سکے تو اس تفاوت کی وجہ سے جب عبد واحد میں مہایات جائز نہیں تو عبدین میں بدرجہ اولی جائز نہ ہوگی کیونکہ یہاں تفاوت اور زیادہ ہے کیونکہ یہاں اعیان جدا جدا ہیں جن میں جلی ہوتا ظاہر ہے۔ مصنف اسی مفہوم کو لان التفاوت فی اعیان الرفیق الخ سے بیان کیا ہے۔
سوال ... آپ نے مہایات فی المنافع کو عبد واحد اور عبدین دونوں میں جائز قرار دیا ہے؟
جواب وہاں ضرورت ہے اور غلہ میں کوئی ضرورت نہیں کیو نکہ کہ منافع نہیں بلکہ مین واحہ پر ہے جس کی خود تقسیم کی جاسکتی ہے کہ وہ دنوں مشترک طور پران کو کرایہ پر دیں اور جو آمدنی ہو اسکو تقسیم کر لیں نیز خدمت کے اندر تفاوت سے دی چشم پوشی سے کام لیتا ہے
Ruling on tahayi' in two slaves for exploitation. Likewise, it is permissible in two slaves according to them (Sahibayn), by analogy with tahayi' in usufruct (manafi'), but not according to him (Abu Hanifa), because disparity in the actual bodies of slaves is greater than disparity in time in a single slave, so it is more appropriate that permissibility is prevented. Tahayi' in service was allowed out of necessity, but there is no necessity in rental income because it can be divided since it is a tangible asset ('ayn). And because the apparent attitude is tolerance in service but strictness in exploitation, so they are not analogous. Translation: Similarly, tahayi' is permissible in two slaves according to the Sahibayn, by analogy with tahayi' in usufruct, but according to Abu Hanifa it is not permissible, because disparity in the actual bodies of slaves is greater. From disparity in time within a single slave, a fortiori, it leads to prevention of permissibility. Tahayi' in service was allowed out of necessity, but there is no necessity in rental income because it can be divided due to the tangible nature of the rent. And because the apparent attitude is tolerance in service and strictness in exploitation, so these two are not analogous. Explanation: Two slaves are jointly owned; each partner takes one for exploitation. This method is only permissible according to the Sahibayn; they analogized exploitation to tahayi' in usufruct. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this tahayi' is not permissible, because if tahayi' in a single slave for successive exploitation is not permissible due to possible disparity in earnings, then a fortiori in two slaves it is not permissible because the disparity is greater due to separate entities. The author expressed this meaning with 'because the disparity in the bodies of slaves...'. Question: You have declared tahayi' in usufruct permissible in both a single slave and two slaves? Answer: There is necessity there, but no necessity in rental income because it is not usufruct but a tangible thing that can be divided; they can jointly rent them out and divide the income. Also, in service, differences are overlooked, but in rental income, strictness prevails.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage details the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tahayi' (apportionment) when two partners own two slaves and wish to divide them for exploitation (e.g., renting them out), each taking one slave. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) permit this by analogy with tahayi' in usufruct (manafi')—like dividing the services of a single slave over time. However, Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits it on three grounds: First, the disparity in value between two distinct slaves is greater than the disparity in earning capacity of a single slave across different times, so if the latter is impermissible, the former is even more so. Second, tahayi' in service (khidmah) was allowed out of necessity because service cannot be physically divided, but rental income (ghallah) can be divided since the rent is tangible property. Third, people are generally lenient in sharing services but strict in monetary matters, so the analogy fails. The commentary also addresses an objection: if tahayi' in a single slave's service is allowed, why not in two slaves for rent? The answer reiterates the necessity argument and the tangible nature of rent.

Key Terms
مہایات (tahayi'): Apportionment of usufruct among co-owners, usually by time or division of the asset's use.
استغلال (istighlal): Exploitation for profit, specifically renting out a slave for income.
عین ('ayn): Tangible property or asset that can be physically divided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is tahayi' in two slaves for rental income not permissible?
A) Because the slaves may run away.
B) Because disparity in value between two slaves is greater than in a single slave's time, and there is no necessity.
C) Because both slaves must be used together.
D) Because the Sahibayn already allowed it.

Key Takeaway
In intra-Hanafi disputes, the difference often hinges on whether qiyas is allowed or overridden by istihsan based on disparity and necessity; the thamarah al-khilaf determines the practical ruling for the mufti.

Tahayi' in Two Animals: Intra-Hanafi Ruling on Rental
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tahayi' of two animals for rental

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on tahayi' in two animals and explain the reasoning by analogy to the riding case.

Core Idea
Tahayi' in two animals for rental is impermissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn permit it.

This brief passage extends the earlier intra-Hanafi dispute on tahayi' in two slaves to two animals (e.g., horses). The same reasoning applies: Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits due to greater disparity and lack of necessity, while the two disciples permit it. The text explicitly refers back to the earlier discussion on riding (rukub), indicating that the analogy is complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is tahayi' (division of usage) of two jointly owned animals for exploitation (istighlal, e.g., renting out). Determine the positions: Abu Hanifa says not permissible; the Sahibayn say permissible.
Note that 'animals' here refers to riding or draft beasts (dābbatayn).
2
Recall the earlier riding case
The text refers back to the case of riding (rukub) where the same dispute occurred. Recall or infer the reasoning: Abu Hanifa's prohibition is based on greater disparity (tafāwut) between the shares and lack of necessity (darūrah), while the Sahibayn permit it considering the ease of division.
The riding case is not reproduced here; it is assumed knowledge from the previous lesson.
3
Apply the analogy
The ruling on animals is analogous to that on slaves because both involve tangible assets with similar potential for inequality. The same 'illah (effective cause) of disparity and necessity applies.
This analogy is a form of qiyās based on the earlier ruling.
4
Note the practical consequence
The ikhtilāf affects whether two joint owners can arrange to alternate exploitation of their animals. Under Abu Hanifa, they must keep undivided or sell; under the Sahibayn, they may divide usage via tahayi'.
The muftā bihī is not specified here; later Hanafi practice may follow the Sahibayn's view for ease.

Tahayi' in Trees and Goats: Ruling on Tangible Yields
Ruling on tahayi' of trees or goats for produce when the yield is tangible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tahayi' for shared trees or goats and explain why tangible yields ('ayn) make it impermissible.

Core Idea
Tahayi' is permissible only for non-enduring usufruct; tangible yields like fruit and milk must be physically divided.

Partners who jointly own trees or goats may consider splitting the animals or trees themselves to avoid dividing the produce. The Hanafi school, however, restricts tahayi' (apportionment) to cases where the benefit is a non-enduring usufruct (manfa'ah), which cannot be physically divided. When the yield is tangible ('ayn), such as fruit or milk, there is no necessity for tahayi', as the yield can be divided directly. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Two partners own trees or goats. They agree that each takes a portion of the trees or goats for themselves to obtain the fruit or milk. The Hanafi ruling is that this tahayi' is not permissible (ghayr jā'iz).
The ruling applies to any tangible yield, not just fruit and milk.
2
Grasp the reasoning (talil)
Tahayi' in usufruct (manfa'ah) was permitted out of necessity because usufruct is an accident ('arad) that does not endure, making division difficult. Fruit and milk, however, are tangible ('ayn) and endure; they can be divided when they exist, so there is no necessity for tahayi'.
'Arad vs 'ayn is the key distinction.
3
Distinguish between permissible and impermissible tahayi'
If the shared property provides a non-enduring benefit (e.g., the shade of a tree, the carrying capacity of an animal), tahayi' may be permissible. If the benefit is tangible and divisible (e.g., fruit, milk, eggs), tahayi' is impermissible.
The default method is to jointly exploit and divide the yield.
4
Apply the principle to new cases
Consider shared cows for milk, poultry for eggs, or land for crops. In each case, if the yield is tangible and divisible, tahayi' is not allowed. Partners must either divide the yield or agree on a different arrangement (e.g., one partner uses the property and compensates the other with a share of the yield).
Consult a scholar for complex modern scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
درختوں اور بکروں کے منافع میں تہا یو کا حکم
ولو كان نخل او شجر او غنم بين اثنين فتهايئا على ان ياخذ كل واحد منهما طائفة يستثمرها اويرعاها ويشرب البانها لا يجوز لان المهاياة في المنافع ضرورة انها لا تبقى فيتعذر قسمتها وهذه اعيان باقية يرد عليها القسمة عند حصولهما
ترجمہ اور اگر درخت کھجور یا اور درخت ہو یا بکری ہو دو آدمیوں کے درمیان پس انہوں نے مہایات کی اس طریقہ پر کہ لے لے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک، ایک حصہ جس سے وہ پھل حاصل کرے یا ان کو چرائے اور ان کا دودھ پیئے تو یہ جائز نہیں اسلئے کہ منافع میں مہایات اس ضرورت سے ہے کہ منافع باقی نہیں رہتے تو ان کی قسمت متعذر ہے اور یہ ( پھل ولبن ) اعیان باقیہ ہیں جن پر ان کے حصوں کے وقت قسمت وارد ہو سکتی ہے۔ تشریح منافع کے اندر مہایات بر بناء ضرورت ہے کہ وہ اعراض ہونے کی وجہ سے باقی نہیں رہ سکتے تو ان کی تقسیم بھی مستعد رہے اور جہاں آمد اعیان میں سے ہو تو وہ پھل درود قسمت ہے تو یہاں کوئی عذر نہیں ہے لہذا یہاں مہایات فی المنافع کی صورت جائز نہ ہوگی جب یہ اصول ذہن نشین ہو گیا تو اب مسئلہ سنئے :- زید اور عمرو کے درمیان کچھ درخت یا بکریاں مشترک ہیں انہوں نے یہ طے کیا کہ کچھ بکریاں زید لے لے اور ان کو چرائے اور دودھ پنے اور کچھ عمر ولے لے اور ایسے ہی درختوں میں تو فرمایا کہ یہ صورت جائز نہیں۔ اسلئے کہ یہاں بکری سے دودھ اور درخت سے پھل حاصل ہوں گے جو عرض نہیں بلکہ عین وجو ہر ہے جس میں بقاء ہے تو ان اعیان کا ہوارہ ہو سکتا ہے تو پھر منافع میں مہایات جائز نہ ہوگی۔
Ruling on tahayi' in the produce of trees and goats. If there are date-palms, trees, or goats between two people, and they make a tahayi' that each one takes a portion to obtain fruit, graze them, and drink their milk, it is not permissible because tahayi' in usufruct is necessary due to the fact that usufruct does not endure, so its division is difficult. These are enduring tangible things (a'yan) that can be divided when they exist. Translation: And if there are date-palms, other trees, or goats between two people, and they make a tahayi' that each one takes a portion to obtain fruit, graze them, and drink their milk, it is not permissible because tahayi' in usufruct is out of necessity: usufruct does not endure, so its division is difficult. These (fruit and milk) are enduring tangible things that can be divided when they exist. Explanation: Tahayi' in usufruct is based on necessity because usufruct, being an accident, does not endure, so its division is difficult. Where the income is from tangible things, the fruit and milk are subject to division, so there is no excuse. Therefore, tahayi' in usufruct is not permissible in this case. Once this principle is understood, listen to the scenario: Zaid and Amr jointly own some trees or goats. They agree that Zaid takes some goats to graze and drink their milk, and Amr takes the others, and similarly with trees. The ruling is that this is not permissible, because here the yield from goats is milk and from trees is fruit, which are not accidents but rather enduring tangible substances, so they can be divided. Therefore, tahayi' in usufruct is not permissible.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on tahayi' (apportionment) when the shared property produces tangible yields, such as fruit from trees or milk from goats. The key principle is that tahayi' in usufruct (manafi') was allowed only out of necessity, because usufruct is non-enduring and cannot be physically divided. However, when the benefit is a tangible thing ('ayn) that can be divided, there is no necessity, and the partners should simply divide the actual produce. Therefore, if partners own trees or goats and agree to split the trees or goats themselves for the purpose of taking the produce, this is impermissible because the produce (fruit, milk) is a tangible asset that can be divided. The correct method is to jointly exploit and divide the yield.

Key Terms
عین ('ayn): A tangible, enduring entity that can be physically divided, such as fruit or milk.
عرض ('arad): An accident or non-enduring attribute, like usufruct, which cannot be divided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is tahayi' not permissible in trees or goats for fruit and milk?
A) Because the partners cannot agree.
B) Because fruit and milk are tangible and can be divided.
C) Because animals cannot be divided.
D) Because tahayi' is only for services.

Key Takeaway
Tahayi' in shared property is only permissible for non-enduring usufruct; tangible yields must be divided physically.

The Validity of Muzara'ah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and the Operative Fatwa
Definition and intra-Hanafi dispute on sharecropping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on muzara'ah, explain their respective proofs, and identify the mufta bihi position with justification.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah is valid per the Sahibayn; Abu Hanifa deemed it void, but the fatwa follows the Sahibayn due to Ummah practice.

Sharecropping (muzara'ah) is a common agricultural contract where land is provided in exchange for a portion of the harvest. Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). Understanding this dispute and the reasons for adopting the Sahibayn's view is essential for correctly applying the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Define muzara'ah
Identify the linguistic and legal definition of muzara'ah as a contract for cultivation in exchange for a share of the produce (e.g., one-third or one-fourth).
The term is derived from زرع (planting/cultivation).
2
State the two positions
Report that Abu Hanifa rules the contract fasid (invalid), while the Sahibayn rule it ja'iz (valid).
This is a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proofs
Analyze their two main evidences: (1) the Prophet's (ﷺ) practice with the people of Khaybar, and (2) analogy (qiyas) to mudarabah (partnership of capital and labor) based on societal need.
The Khaybar narration is a key dalil naqli.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's proofs
Analyze his counter-arguments: (1) the hadith prohibiting مَخَابَرَة (mukhābarah), (2) analogy to the prohibited قَفِيز الطَّحَّان (miller's measure) due to unknown wage, and (3) reinterpretation of the Khaybar transaction as a sulh (settlement) of jizyah.
Abu Hanifa emphasizes jahalah (uncertainty) as a cause of invalidity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Note the practical consequence: the contract is considered valid and widely practiced. Identify the tarjih: the Sahibayn's view is mufta bihi because the Ummah has acted upon it and it fulfills a pressing need.
The commentary explicitly states that Abu Hanifa's view is matruk (abandoned) in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المزارعة
ترجمہ اس کتاب میں زمین کو بٹائی پر دینے کے احکام بیان کیئے جائیں گے
كتاب المزارعة
تشریح کتاب القسمۃ اور کتاب المزارعت میں مناسبت ظاہر ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں بھی زمین کی پیداوار تقسیم کی جاتی ہے۔ مزارعت زرع سے ماخوذ ہے جس کے معنی ہیں القاء الحب ونحوہ فی الارض، اور مفاعلت کبھی صرف ایک کے کام کیلئے بھی مستعمل ہوتا ہے مداواة، معالجة فلا اشكال فيه -
مزارعت کا لغوی اور شرعی معنیٰ ، امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے اقوال
قال ابو حنيفة المزارعة بالثلث والربع باطلة اعلم ان المزارعة لغة مفاعلة من الزرع وفي الشريعة هي عقد على الزرع ببعض الخارج وهي فاسدة عند ابي حنيفة وقالا جائزة لما روى ان النبي عليه السلام عامل اهل خيبر على نصف ما يخرج من ثمر او زرع
ترجمہ ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ تہائی اور چوتھائی پر مزارعت باطل ہے جان لو کہ مزارعت باعتبار لغت زریح سے مفاعلت ( کا مصدر ) ہے اور شریعت میں مزارعت پیداوار کے بعض حصہ پر کھیتی کرنے کا عقد کرنا ہے اور یہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک فاسد ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ جائز ہے اس دلیل سے جو مروی ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے اہل خیبر سے معاملہ فرمایا اس مقدار کے نصف پر جو پھل یا کھیتی سے پیدا ہو۔ تشریح امام ابو حنیفہ مزارعت کو فاسد قرار دیتے ہیں تثلث اور ربع کی قید بر بناء عادت عامہ ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے مزارعت کے لغوی اور شرعی معنی بیان کیئے جو ظاہر ہیں۔
صاحبین نے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فعل سے استدلال کیا ہے کہ جب آپ نے خیبر کو فتح کیا تو وہاں کے یہود کو ان کی زمین پر برقرار رکھا اور یہ طے فرما دیا کہ جو پیداوار ہو اس کا نصف مسلمانوں کو دیا کریں اگر مزارعت جائز نہ ہوتی تو حضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کیوں اس کو اختیار فرماتے ۔ تنبیہ امام ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مزارعت میں زمین کی پیداوار کے بعض حصہ پر کاشتکار کو اجیر رکھنا ہے اور یہ نقل و عقلا ممنوع ہے۔ دلیل نقلی حدیث میں قیز الطحان سے منع فرمایا گیا ہے اور مزارعت بھی اس کے معنی میں ہے۔ دلیل عقلی . اس میں اجارہ کا بدل مجہول ہے اور حضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا عمل اہل خیبر کے ساتھ جزیہ پر محمول ہے نہ کہ مزارعت پر۔ مگر امام صاحب کا قول متروک ہے اور امت کا اس پر تعامل ہے اور اسی وجہ سے صاحبین کے قول پر فتویٰ ہے۔ ( کما سیاتی)
صاحبین کی دوسری دلیل
ولانه عقد شركة بين المال والعمل فيجوز اعتبار ابا لمضاربة والجامع دفع الحاجة فان ذا المال قد لا يهتدى الى العمل والقوى عليه لا يجد المال قمست الحاجة الى انعقاد هذا العقد بينهما
كتاب المزارعة
۱۹۲
اشرف الہدایہ ترن اردو ہدایہ
ترجمہ اور اسلئے کہ یہ ( مزارعت ) مال اور کام کے درمیان شرکت کا عقد ہے تو یہ عقد جائز ہوگا۔ مضاربت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور جامع حاجت کو دور کرنا ہے اسلئے کہ مال والا کبھی کام کرنے کی جانب رہنمائی نہیں پاتا اور کام کے او پر قادر مال نہیں پاتا تو حاجت پیش ہو گئی ان دونوں کے درمیان اس عقد کے منعقد ہونے کی جانب ۔
تشریح یہ صاحبین کی دوسری دلیل ہے کہ جس طرح مضاربت جائز ہے مزارعت بھی جائز ہو کیونکہ مضاربت میں ایک کا مال دوسرے کا کام ہوتا اور ایسے ہی مزارعت میں ہوتا ہے اور اس کو مضاربت پر قیاس کرنے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لوگوں کو ان عقود کی حاجت ہے جو ان دونوں میں مشترک ہے لہذا قیاس صحیح ہوگا اور دلیل حاجت یہ ہے کہ بسا اوقات آدمی کے پاس مال ہوتا ہے مگر وہ کام کرنے کا سلیقہ نہیں رکھتا ہے اور دوسرا کام کا سلیقہ رکھتا ہے مگر اس کے پاس مال نہیں تو اگر ان دونوں کو آپس میں نہ جوڑا جائے تو ایک کا مال خالی پڑا رہے اور اس کا سلیقہ بے کار ہو کر رہ جائے تو ضرورت تھی کہ عقد مزارعت کو جائز قرار دیا جائے۔
سوال کا جواب
بخلاف دفع الغنم والدجاج ودود القز معاملة بنصف الزوائد لانه لا اثر هنالك للعمل في تحصيلها فلم يتحقق شركة
ترجمہ بخلاف بکری اور مرغی اور ریشم کے کپڑے دینے کے زوائد کے نصف کے ساتھ معاملہ کرتے ہوئے اس لئے کہ یہاں زوائد کی تحصیل میں عمل کا کوئی اثر نہیں ہے تو یہ شرکت متحقق نہ ہوگی ۔
تشریح یہ ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔
اعتراض یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک کے پاس بکری ہے اور وہ بکری دوسرے کو دیدے کہ اس کو چرائے اور بچہ اور دودھ دونوں کے درمیان مشترک رہے اسی طرح مرغیاں ہیں وہ دوسرے کو دیدے کہ ان کی حفاظت کرے اور انڈے اور بچے دونوں میں مشترک ہوں گے یا ریشمہ کے کیڑے ہوں وہ دوسرے کو دیدے کہ ان کی حفاظت کرے اور جو ریشم تیار ہو وہ دونوں میں مشترک رہے تو اس کو بھی جائز کہنا چاہیئے کہ کا ایک کا مال ہے اور دوسر کلے کام ہے حالانکہ اس کو آپ نے جائز نہیں کہا؟
جواب تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ یہ اعتراض درست نہیں کیوں کہ شرکت میں کام کرنے والے کے کام کا اثر زوائد پر ظاہر ہونا چاہیے اور یہاں دودھ بچے انڈے ریشم میں عامل نے کچھ نہیں لیا بلکہ ان کو مذکورہ حیوانات کا فعل شمار کیا جائے گا کیوں کہ جب درمیان میں فاعل مختار کا فعل حائل ہو گیا تو عامل کی طرف اضافت نہیں ہو سکتی اس لئے یہ عقد شرکت کے تحت داخل ہوں گے۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل
وله ماروى انه عليه السلام نهى عن المخابرة وهى المزارعة ولانه استيجار ببعض ما يخرج من عمله فيكون في معنى قفيز الطحان ولان الاجر مجهول او معدوم وكل ذالك مفسد ومعاملة النبي عليه السلام اهل خيبر كان خراج مقاسمة بطريق المن والصلح وهو جائز
Book of Sharecropping. Translation: In this book, the rulings of giving land on share tenancy will be explained. Book of Sharecropping. Explanation: The connection between the Book of Partition and the Book of Sharecropping is apparent because in this too the produce of the land is divided. Muzara'ah is derived from زرع, which means casting seeds and the like into the earth. And the form مَفاعَلَة is sometimes used for the action of a single person, like مداواة and معالجة, so there is no issue. The lexical and legal meaning of muzara'ah, and the statements of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Abu Hanifa said: Muzara'ah for one-third or one-fourth is void. Know that muzara'ah lexically is مَفاعَلَة from زرع, and in the Sharia it is a contract for cultivation on the basis of a portion of the produce. It is invalid (fasid) according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said it is permissible (ja'iz), based on what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) dealt with the people of Khaybar for half of what comes out of fruit or cultivation. Translation: Abu Hanifa declared muzara'ah on one-third or one-fourth to be void. Know that lexically muzara'ah is from زرع and in the Sharia it is contracting for cultivation on a portion of the produce, and it is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said it is permissible, based on the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) dealt with the people of Khaybar for half of the produce from fruit or cultivation. Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa considers muzara'ah invalid; the mention of one-third and one-fourth is based on common practice. And according to the Sahibayn it is permissible. The author of Hidayah explained the lexical and legal meanings, which are apparent. The Sahibayn argued from the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that when he conquered Khaybar, he left the Jews on their land and stipulated that half of the produce be given to the Muslims. If muzara'ah were not permissible, why would the Prophet (peace be upon him) do it? Note: Imam Abu Hanifa says that in muzara'ah, the cultivator is hired for a portion of the produce, and this is prohibited textually and rationally. Textual proof: The hadith prohibits قَفِيز الطَّحَّان (the miller's measure), and muzara'ah falls under its meaning. Rational proof: The hire (ujr) is unknown (majhool). And the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) with the people of Khaybar is interpreted as jizyah (tribute), not as muzara'ah. However, the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa is abandoned (matruk), and the Ummah has practiced on the contrary, and for this reason fatwa is given on the statement of the Sahibayn (as will come). The Second Proof of the Sahibayn: And because it is a contract of partnership (shirkah) between capital and labor, so it is permissible, analogizing to mudarabah. The commonality is meeting a need, for the owner of wealth may not be guided to work, and the one capable of work may not find capital, so need necessitates the conclusion of this contract between them. Translation: And because it (muzara'ah) is a contract of partnership between capital and labor, so this contract will be permissible, by analogy to mudarabah. And the commonality is meeting a need, because the wealthy person sometimes is not guided to work, and the one capable of work does not find capital, so the need arises for this contract to be concluded between them. Explanation: This is the second proof of the Sahibayn: Just as mudarabah is permissible, muzara'ah should also be permissible, because in mudarabah one provides capital and the other labor, and similarly in muzara'ah. The reason for analogizing it to mudarabah is that people have a need for these contracts which are common between them, so the analogy is correct. The proof of need is that sometimes a person has wealth but lacks the skill to work, and another has skill but no wealth. If the two are not connected, one's wealth remains idle and the other's skill is wasted. So it was necessary to declare the contract of muzara'ah permissible. Answer to an Objection: Contrary to the case of giving sheep, chickens, and silkworms in exchange for half of the increase (zuwa'id), because there the labor has no effect in obtaining the increase, so partnership (shirkah) is not realized. Translation: As opposed to giving sheep, chickens, and silkworms in a transaction for half of the increase, because there the labor has no effect in obtaining the increase, so partnership is not realized. Explanation: This is an answer to an objection. Objection: If one has a sheep and gives it to another to graze, and the offspring and milk are shared between them; similarly chickens, giving them to another for care, and the eggs and chicks are shared; or silkworms, giving them to another for care, and the silk produced is shared – should these also be considered permissible? Because one provides capital and the other labor. Yet you have not declared them permissible. Answer: The response is that this objection is not correct, because in partnership the worker's labor must have an apparent effect on the increase. Here, in milk, offspring, eggs, and silk, the worker has done nothing; rather these are attributed to the actions of the animals. Since the act of an autonomous agent (فاعل مختار) intervenes, they cannot be attributed to the worker. Therefore, these contracts do not fall under the category of partnership. The Proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: And he has the proof that it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited المخابرة, which is muzara'ah. And because it is hiring (استيجار) for part of what comes out of his work, so it falls under the meaning of قفيز الطحان (the miller's measure). And because the wage (اجر) is unknown (مجهول) or non-existent (معدوم), and all that invalidates (مفسد). And the transaction of the Prophet (peace be upon him) with the people of Khaybar was a division of land-tax (خراج مقاسمة) through favor and conciliation (صلح), and that is permissible.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah, addresses the legal status of muzara'ah (sharecropping) – a contract where an owner gives land to a cultivator in exchange for a share of the produce, typically one-third or one-fourth. The commentary first defines the term linguistically and legally, then presents the central intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that such a contract is fasid (invalid), while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), rule that it is ja'iz (permissible). The Sahibayn base their ruling on the prophetic precedent of the treaty with Khaybar, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) contracted with the Jews for half the produce. They also draw an analogy (qiyas) to mudarabah (silent partnership), arguing that both involve a partnership between capital and labor to fulfill a social need. Abu Hanifa counters with a hadith prohibiting المخابرة (mukhābarah), which is synonymous with muzara'ah, and likens it to the prohibition of قفيز الطحان (engaging a miller with an unknown measure of grain). He argues that the wage is unknown (majhool), rendering the contract analogous to invalid hiring. He interprets the Khaybar incident as a peaceful settlement (sulh) of jizyah rather than a basis for sharecropping. The commentary notes that despite Abu Hanifa's reasoning, his view is considered abandoned (matruk) in practice, and the fatwa is given on the Sahibayn's position due to the consensus of the Ummah and the need for such contracts, especially in agricultural economies. The passage also addresses an objection regarding animals: if sharecropping is valid, why not similar arrangements for sharing the offspring of sheep, chickens, or silkworms? The response distinguishes that in those cases, the labor of the worker does not directly cause the increase; it is the independent action of the animals. Thus, partnership is not realized. This clarifies the scope of muzara'ah: it is valid only where the human effort directly contributes to the produce.

Key Terms
المزارعة (al-muzāra‘ah): A contract on the land for cultivation in exchange for a share of the produce (e.g., one-third or one-fourth).
المخابرة (al-mukhābarah): Synonym for muzara'ah (sharecropping), used in a hadith prohibiting it.
قفيز الطحان (qafīz al-ṭaḥḥān): The miller's measure – an invalid hiring where the wage is a specific measure of grain from the grinding, analogized to muzara'ah by Abu Hanifa.
مفاعلة (mufā‘alah): A verbal form implying mutual action, but here used for a single person's action (like مداواة and معالجة) to avoid objection about the form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract?
A) Batil (void)
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Ja'iz (valid)
D) Haram (unlawful)

Key Takeaway
Muzara'ah is valid in the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's permissibility due to prophetic practice and social necessity.

Abu Hanifa's Proofs Against Muzara'ah and Refutation of Sahibayn's Khaybar Argument
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Muzara'ah prohibition with proofs and counter-arguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's three proofs against Muzara'ah, explain the Hanafi response to Sahibayn's Khaybar argument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds Muzara'ah invalid due to analogy to Mukhabarah and uncertain wage; Sahibayn uphold it by Khaybar practice.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of Muzara'ah (sharecropping). Imam Abu Hanifa argues it is invalid based on a hadith prohibiting Mukhabarah, analogy to an invalid milling contract, and uncertainty of the wage. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) counter with the Prophet's practice at Khaybar. The passage also addresses a later critique questioning the interpretation of the Khaybar arrangement. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists balance textual evidence, analogy, and public practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the parties
What is the legal question? Who are the disputing Imams within the Hanafi school? Recognize that Abu Hanifa declares Muzara'ah fasid, while Sahibayn consider it valid.
2
State Abu Hanifa's three proofs
List the three arguments: (1) Hadith prohibiting Mukhabarah, which he equates to Muzara'ah; (2) Qiyas to the invalid contract of hiring a miller (qir tahan) for a share of flour; (3) The wage being unknown (jahalah) if crop grows or non-existent (ma'dum) if crop fails, which invalidates the hire contract.
The commentary notes that the hadith is from Muslim and that the analogy is jaliy.
3
Analyse Sahibayn's Khaybar argument
Sahibayn rely on the Prophet's arrangement with the Jews of Khaybar, where half the produce was given to the workers. They consider this a valid Muzara'ah contract. Identify the key elements: no fixed term, continuous distribution.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) from the Prophet's practice.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's response to the Khaybar argument
Abu Hanifa's followers argue that the Khaybar arrangement was not a contract but a tax (kharaj muqasamah) done as a favor and reconciliation, not a hire. The lack of a fixed term proves it was not Muzara'ah. Also, the Prophet could have taken all the land but chose to give half as ihsan.
The commentary later notes a counter-argument: the continuous distribution among mujahideen suggests it was Muzara'ah, as in Sahihayn.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
What is the difference in outcome? Under Abu Hanifa, if a Muzara'ah contract is made, it is fasid and the worker gets ujr al-mithl (market wage). Under Sahibayn, it is valid and the agreed share is binding. Note that the mufta bihi today is Sahibayn's view due to public need.
This illustrates how later practice (taamul) can override qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المزارعة
ترجمہ او ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل وہ ہے جو مروی ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے مخابرہ سے منع فرمایا اور یہ مزارعت ہے اور اس لئے کہ یہ اجیر رکھنا ہے اس پیداوار کے بعض کے ساتھ جو اس کے عمل سے پیدا ہو تو یہ قضیر بطحان کے معنی میں ہو جائے گا اور اس لئے کہ اجرت مجہول یا معدوم ہے اور یہ تمام مفسد ہیں اور نبی علیہ السلام کا معاملہ اہل خیبر سے وہ خراج مقاسمت تھا احسان و مصالحت کے طریقہ پر اور وہ جائز ہے۔ تشریح بی امام ابوحنیفہ کے دلائل ہیں جن کو ماقبل میں بھی اختصار ابیان کر دیا گیا ہے۔ - حدیث میں مزارعت سے منع کیا گیا ہے بھی النبي عليه السلام المخابرة، اخرجهہ مسلم اور مخابر و اوریا قلہ مزارعت ہی کو کہا جاتا ہے قلت یہاں رافع بن خدیج اور دو آدمیوں کے جھگڑے پر غور نہیں فرمایا جن کے جواب میں آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مزارعت سے منع فرمایا تھا جس کی تفصیل عروہ ابن زبیر کی حدیث میں ہے نصب الرایہ ص ۸۰ ج ۴ پر اس حدیمہ کے متعدد جوابات دیئے گئے ہیں۔ -۲- یہ فیز طحان کے درجہ میں ہے جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے سو چکی والا آٹا پیسے اور غلہ والا پانی کی اجرت اسی آٹے میں سے دے مثلاً دسواں وغیرہ تو یہ جائز نہیں۔ کیوں کہ اصول یہ ہے کہ اجیر جو کام کرنے اس کی مزدوری اس میں سے مقرر نہ کی جائے اور مزارعت میں یہی صورت ہے قلت قیر طحان کا عدم جواز منصوص علیہ ہے اور مقیس منصوص علیہ نہیں ہے اور امت کا اس پر تعامل ہے اور غیر منصوص علیہ میں امت کا تعامل جواز کی دلیل ہے۔ ۳- اگر پیداوار ہو تو اجرت مجہول ہے اس لئے کہ معلوم نہیں کہ کتنی پیداوار ہوتی اور اگر پیداوار نہ ہو تو اجرت معدوم ہے اور اجرت کی جہالت یا اجرت کا نہ ہونا مفسد اجارہ ہے قلت ، یہ جہالت وغیرہ مضاربت میں بھی موجود ہے پھر اس کو بھی نا جائز ہونا چاہیے نیز یہ یا کا نہ ہونا مضر ہے یہ وغیر و میں ہی موجود ہے پر اس کوئی ناجائز ہونا نیز یہ انتہاء شرکت ہے جس میں مذکورہ جہالت وغیر ہ مفسد نہیں۔ - صاحبین نے اہل خیر کے واقعہ سے جو استدلال کیا تھا اس کا جواب دیا گیا کہ یہ مزارعت نہیں تھی بلکہ خراج مقاسمت تھا اور امام کو اختیار ہے کہ خراج موظف اور مقاسمت میں جو لینا چاہے اختیار کرے اور یہ آپ نے ان پر احسان فرمایا تھا ورنہ ساری زمین بھی لے سکتے تھے ۔ نیز مدت مقرر نہ کرنا اس کی واضح دلیل ہے کہ یہ خراج تھا نہ کہ مزارعت ۔ قلت خیبر میں مجاہدین کے حصول کا جاری ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ خراج نہیں تھا بلکہ مزارعت تھی اور صحیحین میں بروایت ابن عمر اس میں حصہ جاری ہونا مصرح ہے۔
The Book of Muzara'ah. Translation: And Abu Hanifa's proof is that which is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited al-mukhabarah, and this is muzara'ah, and because it is hiring for a portion of the produce that results from his labor, so it becomes like the meaning of qir tahan, and because the wage is unknown or non-existent, and all these are invalidating factors. And the Prophet's dealing with the people of Khaybar was kharaj muqasamah on the basis of favor and reconciliation, and that is permissible. Commentary: These are the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa which were also summarized earlier. - The hadith prohibits muzara'ah: the Prophet (SAW) prohibited al-mukhabarah, narrated by Muslim, and mukhabarah is called muzara'ah. I say: Here the incident of Rafi' ibn Khadij and two men is not considered...
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on Muzara'ah. Imam Abu Hanifa argues for its prohibition using three proofs: (1) a hadith prohibiting Mukhabarah (which he equates to Muzara'ah), (2) analogy to qir tahan (hiring a miller for a share of flour) which is invalid, and (3) the wage being either unknown (if crop grows) or non-existent (if no crop) which nullifies the hire contract. The commentary then addresses Sahibayn's reliance on the Khaybar incident: Abu Hanifa's followers interpret it as kharaj muqasama (a tax on produce) done as a favor, not a contract, evidenced by the lack of a fixed term. However, the author notes a counter-argument: the continuous distribution of shares in Khaybar among the mujahideen indicates it was Muzara'ah, as recorded in Sahih Bukhari and Sahih Muslim. This dispute illustrates the tension between textual evidence and public practice in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzāra‘ah): Contract where one provides land, another labor, sharing the produce by agreed fraction.
مخابرة (mukhābarah): Term in hadith prohibition; equated with Muzara'ah by Abu Hanifa.
قير طحان (qīr ṭaḥān): Hiring a miller for a share of flour; used as analogy by Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

What was the primary proof used by Abu Hanifa to argue against the validity of Muzara'ah?
A) The Hadith prohibiting Mukhabarah
B) The practice of the Prophet in Khaybar
C) The consensus of the four caliphs
D) The Quranic verse on contracts

Key Takeaway
The dispute over Muzara'ah shows how Qiyas and Hadith can be countered by practice and Istihsan in Hanafi fiqh.

Compensation in Fasid Muzara'ah Without Crop
Ruling on compensation when invalid Muzara'ah yields no produce, with details based on seed ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the compensation rules for a fasid Muzara'ah contract when no crop is produced, distinguishing based on seed ownership.

Core Idea
Produce belongs to seed owner; worker gets ujr al-mithl for labor or pays ujr al-mithl for land.

When a Muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract is invalid (fasid) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and no crop results, the compensation depends on who provided the seeds. This lesson clarifies the two possible scenarios and the legal reasoning behind allocating wages and produce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Recognize that the Muzara'ah is fasid (voidable) under Abu Hanifa's ruling; the contract is invalid but actions performed under it have legal consequences.
This ruling applies only when no crop is produced.
2
Determine seed ownership
Check whether the seed was provided by the landowner or the worker. This is the decisive factor for compensation.
Seed ownership determines the produce's owner and who receives ujr al-mithl.
3
Apply compensation rule for landowner's seed
If the landowner provided the seed, the worker receives ujr al-mithl (equivalent wage) for his labor, as the contract is treated like a fasid hire.
The worker does not pay for land use.
4
Apply compensation rule for worker's seed
If the worker provided the seed, he must pay the landowner ujr al-mithl for the use of the land; the produce (if any) belongs to the worker as seed owner.
The produce is the growth of the seed owner's property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا فسدت عنده فان سقى الارض وكربها ولم يخرج شئ فله اجر مثله لانه في معنى إجارة فاسدة وهذا اذا كان البذر من قبل صاحب الارض وان كان البذر من قبله فعليه اجر مثل الارض والخارج في الوجهين لصاحب البذر لانه نماء ملكه وللاخر الاجر كما فصلنا
ترجمہ اور مزارعت جبکہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک فاسد ہے تو اگر عامل نے زمیں کو سیراب کیا ہو اور اس میں ہل چلایا ہو اور کچھ پیداوار نہ ہو تو اس کے لئے اس کے مثل کا اجر ہے اس لئے کہ یہ اجارہ فاسدہ کے معنی میں ہے اور یہ جب ہے جبکہ بیج زمین والے کی جانب سے ہو اور اگر بیج کام کرنے والے کی طرف سے ہو تو اس پر زمین کے مثل کی اجرت ہوگی اور یہ پیداوار دونوں صورتوں میں بیج والے کی ہے اس لئے کہ یہ اس کی ملک کی بڑھوتری ہے اور دوسرے کے لئے اجرت ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے تفصیل بیان کی۔
تشریح امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مزارعت تو فاسد ہوتی ہے اگر دو شخصوں نے عقد مزارعت کیا اور کاشت کار نے محنت کی اور پیداوار کچھ نہ ہوئی تو اس کو اجرت مثلیہ ملے گی اس لئے کہ یہ اجارہ فاسدہ ہے اور اجارہ فاسدہ میں اجیر کو اجر مثل ماتا ہے لہذا یہاں بھی ملے گا یعنی اس صورت میں جب کہ بیج زمین کے مالک نے ڈالا ہو۔ اور اگر بیج کا شتکار کا ہوتو پیداوار کا شتکار کی ہوگی اور زمین والے کو اس کی زمین کا کرایہ دیا جائے گا خلاصہ کلام پیچ جس کا ہو گا اس کی پیداوار ہوگی۔
And when it [Muzara'ah] is invalid according to him [Abu Hanifa], then if the worker irrigated the land and tilled it and nothing came out, he has the ujr al-mithl (equivalent wage) because it is in the meaning of a fasid hire contract. And this is when the seed is from the landowner's side. And if the seed is from his [the worker's] side, then upon him is the ujr al-mithl of the land. And the produce in both cases belongs to the owner of the seed because it is the growth of his property, and the other has the wage as we have detailed. Translation: And if Muzara'ah is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, then if the worker irrigated the land and plowed it and no produce came out, he gets ujr al-mithl because it is like a fasid hire. This is when the seed is from the landowner. And if the seed is from the worker, then he must pay ujr al-mithl of the land, and the produce in both cases belongs to the seed owner because it is the growth of his property, and the other gets the wage. Commentary: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, Muzara'ah is invalid. If two persons made a Muzara'ah contract and the cultivator worked and no produce came out, he gets ujr al-mithl because it is a fasid hire. This applies when the seed was provided by the landowner. If the seed was from the cultivator, the produce belongs to the cultivator, and the landowner gets rent for his land. In summary, the produce goes to the owner of the seed.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Imam Abu Hanifa on the consequences of an invalid (fasid) Muzara'ah contract where no crop is produced. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios based on who provided the seed: (1) If the landowner provided the seed, the worker gets ujr al-mithl (the customary wage for his labor) because the contract is treated as a fasid hire (ijara fasida). (2) If the worker provided the seed, he must pay the landowner ujr al-mithl for the use of the land, and the crop (if any) belongs to the seed owner. The legal reasoning is that the produce is considered the growth (nama') of the seed owner's property, so it belongs to him. The worker's compensation is based on the benefit he received (the use of land or the labor provided). This ruling applies specifically when no crop emerges; if a crop had emerged, the distribution would follow the invalid contract's terms? The text does not elaborate on that scenario. The commentary emphasizes that the produce always belongs to the seed owner, correcting a possible misunderstanding that it goes to the worker.

Key Terms
اجر مثل (ujr al-mithl): The customary or equivalent wage for a similar service in the market; not the agreed-upon wage.
بذر (badhr): The seeds used for planting; ownership of seed is critical in determining ownership of produce and compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The landowner
B) The worker
C) Both equally
D) Neither, as the contract is void

Key Takeaway
In a fasid Muzara'ah, produce belongs to the seed owner, and the other party receives or pays ujr al-mithl based on who provided the seed.

Mufta Bihi: Sahibayn's View on Muzara'ah Due to Custom and Need
Declares the relied-upon position in Muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi ruling on Muzara'ah and explain why customary practice (ta'amul) overrides qiyas in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Customary practice and public need can override qiyas, making Sahibayn's view the operative fatwa.

In the Hanafi school, Muzara'ah (sharecropping) was subject to disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa deemed it invalid (fasid) by qiyas, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, permitted it. This lesson examines the passage from Al-Hidayah that establishes the final relied-upon position (mufta bihi), showing how the principle of ta'amul (established community practice) and necessity tip the scales. You will see how custom can become a source of law that overrides analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling debate
Recognize that the ruling concerns the validity of Muzara'ah (sharecropping). Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Hanifa says invalid, Sahibayn say valid.
The passage begins by stating the fatwa is on Sahibayn's view.
2
Extract the reason for tarjih
Find the two grounds given: (1) people's need (hajat al-nas) and (2) the manifest practice of the Ummah (zuhr ta'amul al-ummah).
Both are independent justifications.
3
Analyze the principle: qiyas is left due to practice
The passage states 'al-qiyas yutraku bi al-ta'amul' – qiyas is abandoned because of practice. This is a key usul principle.
This shows that custom (urf) can override qiyas.
4
Compare with Istisna' as a precedent
The commentator draws a parallel to Istisna' (manufacturing contract), which also violates qiyas (sale of non-existent item) but is permitted due to universal practice.
This reinforces the principle and shows consistency.
5
Conclude: the mufta bihi and its authority
State that the mufta bihi is Sahibayn's view of validity (ja'iz). The authority is later Hanafi jurists (fatawa mutakhkhirin) who preferred this due to need and practice.
This demonstrates how fatwa evolves with societal needs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الا ان الفتوى على قولهما لحاجة الناس اليها ولظهور تعامل الامة بها والقياس يترك بالتعامل كما في الاستصناع.
ترجمہ مگر تحقیق کہ فتویٰ صاحبین کے قول پر ہے مزارعت کی جانب لوگوں کی حاجت لوگوں کی حاجت کی وجہ سے اور اس پر امت کے تعامل کی وجہ سے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا جاتا ہے جیسے استصناع میں۔
تشریح اس کی تفصیل ظاہر ہے صاحبین کے نزدیک حدیث نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مقابل کی دلیل کو قیاس سے تعبیر کیا گیا ہے۔ استصناع ، مثلاً کسی کا ریگر سے کہا کہ میرے لئے جو تا بنا دے اتنے روپے میں تو یہ جائز ہے حالانکہ اس کے اندر معدوم کی بیچ ہے جو جائز نہیں لیکن اس پر امت کا تعامل ہے جس کی وجہ سے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا گیا ایسے ہی مزارعت میں بھی ہوگا۔
Except that the fatwa is upon their statement [Sahibayn] due to the people's need for it and due to the manifest practice of the Ummah with it, and qiyas is abandoned due to practice, as in the case of istisna'. Translation: But verily the fatwa is on the statement of the two (Sahibayn) because of the people's need for Muzara'ah and because of the practice of the Ummah, so qiyas is abandoned due to practice, as in istisna'. Commentary: The detail is clear: according to Sahibayn, because there is no hadith [against Muzara'ah], the opponent's proof is considered qiyas. Istisna', for example, a person says to a craftsman 'make me a pair of shoes for such amount' – this is valid despite involving a sale of a non-existent item, but the practice of the Ummah has permitted it, so qiyas is abandoned. Similarly for Muzara'ah.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage provides the final operative ruling (mufta bihi) on Muzara'ah within the Hanafi school. Although Imam Abu Hanifa held Muzara'ah to be invalid based on qiyas (analogy to prohibited Mukhabarah, miller hire, etc.), the fatwa is given according to the view of Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) who permitted it. The reason is twofold: (1) people are in dire need of Muzara'ah as a means of agricultural production, and (2) the Ummah has continuously practiced it throughout the ages, establishing it as an accepted custom ('urf and ta'amul). The principle invoked is that established practice (ta'amul) overrides qiyas (analogical reasoning). The commentary draws a parallel to the contract of Istisna' (manufacturing order), where selling an item not yet in existence is normally invalid by qiyas, but the practice of the Ummah has made it permissible. Thus, Muzara'ah is given the same treatment: the strong custom of sharecropping justifies setting aside the strict analogy. This illustrates the Hanafi methodology of using istihsan (juristic preference) based on custom and need to override strict qiyas.

Key Terms
تعامل (ta‘āmul): The established practice of the Muslim community (Ummah) that serves as a basis for overriding qiyas.
استصناع (istiṣnā‘): A contract of manufacturing where one party orders a specific item to be made, involving sale of a non-existent object; used as a parallel for overriding qiyas by practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the fatwa on Muzara'ah given according to Sahibayn's view?
A) Because Abu Hanifa's hadith is weak
B) Because of people's need and continuous practice of the Ummah
C) Because Sahibayn had stronger qiyas
D) Because the Quran explicitly allows it

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, established customary practice (ta'amul) and necessity can override strict qiyas, an application of istihsan that yields the operative fatwa for Muzara'ah as valid.

First Condition for Valid Muzara'ah: Land Must Be Arable
Stipulates the requirement that land must be suitable for cultivation for Muzara'ah to be valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for a valid Muzara'ah contract and identify which types of land invalidate the contract.

Core Idea
A Muzara'ah contract is only valid if the land can grow crops.

This lesson focuses on the very first condition that must be met for a Muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract to be valid according to the Hanafi scholars who permit it. The condition is simple yet essential: the land must be arable. Without this, the entire purpose of the contract—to produce a crop—cannot be achieved, rendering the agreement invalid. We will explore which lands fail this condition and why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the Arabic text and locate the phrase stating the condition. The text says 'one of them is that the land is suitable for cultivation'.
The condition is explicitly stated as the first of eight conditions for validity.
2
Understand the rationale
The text gives the reason: 'because the purpose is not achieved without it'. The purpose of Muzara'ah is to produce crops; uncultivable land defeats this purpose.
This rationale helps in understanding why the condition is necessary.
3
Identify excluded land types
The commentary specifies two types of land that are not arable: saline (salty) land and swampy (waterlogged) land. These cannot sustain crops.
Memorize these examples as they appear in classical texts.
4
Note the legal context
This condition applies only according to those who permit Muzara'ah (Sahibayn – Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Imam Abu Hanifa considered Muzara'ah invalid in principle, so this condition is for the mufta bihi view.
Understanding the ikhtilaf is important for a complete picture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المزارعة لصحتها على قول من يجيزها شروط احدها كون الارض صالحة للزراعة لان المقصود لا يحصل دونه
ترجمہ پھر مزارعت اس کی صحت کے لئے اس شخص کے قول پر جو اس کو جائز قرار دیتا ہے چند شرطیں ہیں ان میں سے ایک زمین کا کاشت کے قابل ہونا اس لئے کہ مقصود اس کے بغیر حاصل نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح مزارعت کی صحت کے لئے آٹھ شرطیں ہیں یعنی ان لوگوں کے نزدیک جو مزارعت کو جائز کہتے ہیں ان کے نزدیک بھی آٹھ شرطیں میں پہلی شرط زمین کا قابل کاشت ہوتا ہے لہذا دلال والی زمین اور جس میں سے پانی رس کر بہتا ہو اس میں مزارعت صحیح نہیں ہے۔
تنبیہ امام صاحب نے مزارعت سے شدت سے منع نہیں فرمایا ہے اور بقول امام محمد امام صاحب نے مزارعت میں جو جزئیات متفرعہ
Then, for the validity of Muzara'ah according to the one who permits it, there are conditions. One of them is that the land is suitable for cultivation because the purpose is not achieved without it. Translation: Then for the validity of Muzara'ah according to the one who permits it, there are several conditions. Among them is that the land is arable, because the purpose is not attained without it. Commentary: There are eight conditions for the validity of Muzara'ah, i.e., according to those who say it is permissible. The first condition is that the land is arable. Hence, land that is saline or swampy (where water seeps and flows) is not valid for Muzara'ah. Note: Imam [Abu Hanifa] did not prohibit Muzara'ah strictly; and according to Imam Muhammad, Imam [Abu Hanifa] [had] many derivative details regarding Muzara'ah.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage outlines the first condition for a valid Muzara'ah contract according to those scholars (like Sahibayn) who consider it permissible. The condition is that the land must be fit for agriculture (saliha li al-zira'ah). The rationale is straightforward: the entire purpose of Muzara'ah is to produce a crop, and if the land is barren, saline, or waterlogged such that cultivation is impossible, the contract's objective cannot be achieved. The commentary specifies that land which is 'dallal' (saline/salty) or land where water seeps and flows continuously (swampy) is not suitable, and thus Muzara'ah on such land is not valid. The note (tanbih) adds an important nuance: Imam Abu Hanifa did not prohibit Muzara'ah severely (shiddatan), implying that his position might be softer than some other hadith-based prohibitions. It also mentions that according to Imam Muhammad, Imam Abu Hanifa had detailed subsidiary rulings on Muzara'ah, indicating that he did not completely dismiss the topic despite considering the basic contract invalid. This condition applies even for those who permit Muzara'ah; it is a prerequisite for the contract to be sound.

Key Terms
صالح للزراعة (ṣāliḥ lil-zirā‘ah): Suitable for cultivation; land that can produce crops through normal agricultural processes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The land must be arable
C) The landowner must be present
D) A fixed term must be set

Key Takeaway
For a Muzara'ah contract to be valid (according to those who permit it), the land must be capable of producing crops; saline and waterlogged lands are explicitly excluded.

Ruling on Invalid Muzara'ah and Fatwa on Sahibayn's View
Ruling on fasid muzara'ah and adoption of Sahibayn's fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the compensation rules in a fasid muzara'ah and EXPLAIN why the mufta bihi position follows the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah is valid in the Hanafi fatwa because necessity and custom override strict qiyas.

In this passage, we explore the Hanafi school's approach to muzara'ah (sharecropping). While Imam Abu Hanifah considers it invalid, the mufta bihi adopts the view of the Sahibayn, allowing it due to the widespread practice and need. Understanding this shift prepares you for how the Hanafi school balances qiyas with custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios based on seed ownership
The text distinguishes between two cases: (1) seed from the landowner, (2) seed from the worker. Determine which party owns the seed, as this determines who gets the produce.
The produce always follows the seed owner.
2
State the compensation rule for each scenario
When the contract is invalid (fasid), the worker receives ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage) if seed is from landowner, or pays land rental if seed is from worker. The produce belongs to the seed owner.
This treats the contract as an invalid lease (ijarah fasidah).
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifah holds muzara'ah as inherently fasid based on qiyas. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it valid due to need and custom.
The disagreement is over the role of qiyas versus ta'amul.
4
Understand the justification for the Sahibayn's view
The text explicitly states that the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view 'الحاجه الناس اليها' (due to people's need) and 'لظهور تعامل الامة' (due to manifest practice of the ummah). Qiyas is abandoned because of custom, as in istisna'.
This is a key Hanafi principle: custom can override qiyas.
5
Apply the principle: custom overrides qiyas
Analogize to istisna' (manufacturing contract): selling a non-existent item is normally prohibited by qiyas, but it is allowed because of continuous practice. Similarly, muzara'ah is allowed.
This illustrates the Hanafi methodology of istihsan and ta'amul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس کے لئے اس کے مثل کا اجر ہے اس لئے کہ یہ اجارہ فاسدہ کے معنی میں ہے اور یہ جب ہے جبکہ بیج زمین والے کی جانب سے ہو اور اگر بیج کام کرنے والے کی طرف سے ہو تو اس پر زمین کے مثل کی اجرت ہوگی اور یہ پیداوار دونوں صورتوں میں بیج والے کی ہے اس لئے کہ یہ اس کی ملک کی بڑھوتری ہے اور دوسرے کے لئے اجرت ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے تفصیل بیان کی۔ تشریح امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مزارعت تو فاسد ہوتی ہے اگر دو شخصوں نے عقد مزارعت کیا اور کاشت کار نے محنت کی اور پیداوار کچھ نہ ہوئی تو اس کو اجرت مثلیہ ملے گی اس لئے کہ یہ اجارہ فاسدہ ہے اور اجارہ فاسدہ میں اجیر کو اجر مثل ماتا ہے لہذا یہاں بھی ملے گا یعنی اس صورت میں جب کہ بیج زمین کے مالک نے ڈالا ہو۔ اور اگر بیج کا شتکار کا ہوتو پیداوار کا شتکار کی ہوگی اور زمین والے کو اس کی زمین کا کرایہ دیا جائے گا خلاصہ کلام پیچ جس کا ہو گا اس کی پیداوار ہوگی۔ مفتی به قول الا ان الفتوى على قولهما لحاجة الناس اليها ولظهور تعامل الامة بها والقياس يترك بالتعامل كما في الاستصناع. ترجمہ مگر تحقیق کہ فتویٰ صاحبین کے قول پر ہے مزارعت کی جانب لوگوں کی حاجت لوگوں کی حاجت کی وجہ سے اور اس پر امت کے تعامل کی وجہ سے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا جاتا ہے جیسے استصناع میں۔ تشریح اس کی تفصیل ظاہر ہے صاحبین کے نزدیک حدیث نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مقابل کی دلیل کو قیاس سے تعبیر کیا گیا ہے۔ استصناع ، مثلاً کسی کا ریگر سے کہا کہ میرے لئے جو تا بنا دے اتنے روپے میں تو یہ جائز ہے حالانکہ اس کے اندر معدوم کی بیچ ہے جو جائز نہیں لیکن اس پر امت کا تعامل ہے جس کی وجہ سے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا گیا ایسے ہی مزارعت میں بھی ہوگا۔
For him is the wage of its like, because this is in the meaning of an invalid lease (ijarah fasidah). And this is when the seed is from the landowner. But if the seed is from the worker, then he will pay the landowner the rental value of the land. In both cases, the produce belongs to the one who provided the seed, because it is an increase of his property, and the other's compensation is wages. Commentary: According to Imam Abu Hanifah, muzara'ah is invalid. If two persons contract muzara'ah and the worker labors but no produce results, he receives compensation at the rate of his labor's equivalent (ujrat al-mithl) because it is like an invalid lease where the worker receives ujrat al-mithl. This applies when the seed was from the landowner. If the seed was from the worker, the produce belongs to the worker and he pays the landowner rent. In essence, the produce goes with the seed. Fatwa: But the fatwa is on the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) due to people's need for it and the manifest practice of the ummah, and qiyas is abandoned due to common practice, as in istisna'. Translation: Indeed, the fatwa is on the view of the two (Sahibayn) for muzara'ah because of people's need and the ummah's practice; qiyas is abandoned due to practice, as in istisna'. Commentary: The detail is clear; they refer to the opponent's proof as qiyas due to lack of hadith. Istisna': e.g., someone tells a cobbler: 'Make me shoes for such rupees'; this is permissible even though it involves selling a non-existent item which is not permissible, but the ummah's practice is to allow it, so qiyas is left. Similarly for muzara'ah.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on an invalid (fasid) muzara'ah contract and establishes the fatwa position. It begins by stating the compensation rule: if the seed comes from the landowner, the worker receives ujrat al-mithl (compensation equivalent to his labor) because the contract is treated as an invalid lease. If the seed is from the worker, the worker gets the produce and pays the landowner the rental value of the land. The produce always follows the seed. The commentary explains Imam Abu Hanifah's view that muzara'ah is fundamentally fasid. Then the text presents the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position: the fatwa is on the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), who permit muzara'ah based on necessity (hajah) and the continuous practice (ta'amul) of the ummah. Qiyas (analogy) would disallow it, but it is set aside for common practice, similar to the contract of istisna' (manufacturing order) where selling a non-existent item is normally impermissible but allowed due to custom. This shows the Hanafi method of giving weight to 'urf and necessity over strict qiyas.

Key Terms
مزارعت (muzāra‘ah): Sharecropping contract: owner of land gives it to a worker for cultivation in return for a share of the produce.
اجرت مثلیہ (ujrat al-mithl): Compensation equivalent to the prevailing wage for similar labor, not a predetermined amount.
تعامل (ta‘āmul): Widespread and continuous practice among Muslims, considered a basis for ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an invalid muzara'ah where the worker labors but no produce is harvested, and the seed was from the landowner, what does the worker receive?
A) Nothing, because the contract is invalid
B) Ujrat al-mithl (compensation for his labor)
C) Full market rent of the land
D) A share of the expected produce

Key Takeaway
Muzara'ah is valid per the Hanafi fatwa because necessity and custom override strict qiyas.
