First Condition for Valid Muzara'ah: Land Must Be Arable
First condition for valid muzara'ah: land must be arable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for a valid muzara'ah contract, identify land types that violate it, and explain the rationale ('illa) behind the condition.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah requires arable land; otherwise the contract's purpose is defeated.

In this lesson, we examine the first of eight conditions for a valid muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract according to the Hanafi school. The condition is straightforward: the land must be capable of producing crops. We will explore why this condition is essential and what types of land fail it. We also touch on an important intra-madhhab nuance: Imam Abu Hanifah's own view was that muzara'ah is invalid, yet he still outlined conditions for validity knowing people would need them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Find the phrase in the Arabic text: 'كون الارض صالحة للزراعة' (the land being suitable for cultivation). This is the first condition.
It is a shart (condition) for validity.
2
Understand the rationale ('illa)
The text gives the 'illa: 'لان المقصود لا يحصل دونه' (because the purpose is not achieved without it). The purpose of muzara'ah is to produce crops, so non-arable land defeats the contract's object.
This is a talil (causal reasoning).
3
Recognize exceptions (mawani')
The commentary specifies that saline (dallal) land or land with excessive water seepage is not suitable. These are mawani' (preventers) that block validity.
Such land makes the muzara'ah contract batil (void).
4
Note the intra-madhhab context
The Tanbih (note) explains that Imam Abu Hanifah (according to his student Imam Muhammad) personally considered muzara'ah invalid, but he still laid down conditions 'according to the one who permits it' (i.e., the Sahibayn). This shows the school's practical accommodation of 'urf (custom).
The mufta bihi (operative) position follows the Sahibayn, making muzara'ah permissible with these conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مزارعت کی صحت کیلئے آٹھ شرائط میں سے پہلی شرط ثم المزارعة لصحتها على قول من يجيزها شروط احدها كون الارض صالحة للزراعة لان المقصود لا يحصل دونه ترجمہ پھر مزارعت اس کی صحت کے لئے اس شخص کے قول پر جو اس کو جائز قرار دیتا ہے چند شرطیں ہیں ان میں سے ایک زمین کا کاشت کے قابل ہونا اس لئے کہ مقصود اس کے بغیر حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح مزارعت کی صحت کے لئے آٹھ شرطیں ہیں یعنی ان لوگوں کے نزدیک جو مزارعت کو جائز کہتے ہیں ان کے نزدیک بھی آٹھ شرطیں میں پہلی شرط زمین کا قابل کاشت ہوتا ہے لہذا دلال والی زمین اور جس میں سے پانی رس کر بہتا ہو اس میں مزارعت صحیح نہیں ہے۔ تنبیہ امام صاحب نے مزارعت سے شدت سے منع نہیں فرمایا ہے اور بقول امام محمد امام صاحب نے مزارعت میں جو جزئیات متفرعہ بیان فرما ئیں اور شرنبلالیہ میں خلاصہ سے منقول ہے کہ ان مسائل کو امام صاحب نے متفرع کیا اس شخص کے قول کے مطابق جو اس کو جائز ، قرار دیتا ہے چونکہ امام صاحب کو علم تھا کہ لوگ ان کے اس قول پر عمل نہیں کریں گے۔ شامی ص ۱۷۴ ج ۵
From the eight conditions for the validity of muzara'ah, the first condition: Then muzara'ah, for its validity according to the one who considers it valid, has conditions. One of them is that the land be suitable for cultivation, because the objective is not achieved without it. Translation: Then for muzara'ah, for its validity according to the one who permits it, there are conditions. One of them is that the land be fit for cultivation, because the purpose will not be attained without it. Commentary: For the validity of muzara'ah, there are eight conditions, i.e., according to those who consider it valid, among the eight conditions the first is that the land be arable. Therefore, saline land or land where water seeps through is not valid for muzara'ah. Note: Imam Abu Hanifah did not strictly prohibit muzara'ah; according to Imam Muhammad, Imam Abu Hanifah derived these subsidiary issues in accordance with the view of the one who permits it, because he knew that people would not act on his own view. Commentary
This passage begins the discussion of conditions for a valid muzara'ah contract according to those who permit it (primarily the Sahibayn and the mufta bihi position). The first condition is that the land must be physically capable of producing crops. The Arabic matn states 'كون الارض صالحة للزراعة'—the land must be arable. The 'illa (effective cause) is that the purpose of the contract—cultivation and harvest—cannot be achieved otherwise. The commentary clarifies that saline (dallal) land or land with excessive water seepage is not suitable, so a muzara'ah contract on such land is invalid. The Tanbih (note) adds that Imam Abu Hanifah's own position was that muzara'ah is invalid, but he still outlined conditions for its validity because he knew people would need it and would not follow his stricter view. This shows the Hanafi method of accommodating practical necessity ('urf).

صالحة للزراعة (ṣāliḥah li al-zirā‘ah): Suitable for cultivation; the land must be capable of producing crops.
دلال والی زمین (dallāl wālī zamīn): Saline land that is not cultivable.

Second and Third Conditions: Capable Parties and Specified Duration
Conditions that parties be legally capable and the duration be specified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a valid muzara'ah contract and explain when custom makes explicit duration specification unnecessary.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah requires capable parties and a known duration, but custom can define duration implicitly.

This passage introduces two key conditions for a valid muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract. First, both parties must be legally capable—a requirement for all contracts. Second, the duration must be specified, but the Hanafi school accommodates local custom: if custom renders the duration implicit (e.g., one harvest season), explicit mention is not needed. Let's unpack the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
The passage explicitly states the second condition (parties must be ahl al-'aqd) and the third condition (duration must be specified). Note that these are conditions of validity, not pillars.
2
Understand the universality of the capacity condition
The author notes this condition is not specific to muzara'ah—it applies to all contracts. A party lacking sanity or maturity cannot contract. Consider that even a slave can contract if authorized.
3
Analyze why duration is required
Muzara'ah is a contract on usufruct; the duration is the measure (mi'yar) of the usufruct. Without a known duration, the subject matter is ambiguous, potentially invalidating the contract.
The Arabic text says 'al-muddatu hiya al-mi'yāru lahā'.
4
Recognize the exception for custom
The Tanbih (note) says that in some lands (biladuna), the duration is not specified because custom fixes it (e.g., one harvest). This is the mufta bihi position. Imam Muhammad only required explicit duration in Kufa because seasons varied.
This shows the Hanafi use of 'urf (custom) to relax a condition.
5
Synthesize the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Muhammad held that explicit duration is necessary; later scholars (including the author of Durr Mukhtar) followed the fatwa that custom can replace explicit mention. The practical difference: in regions with a fixed custom, specifying duration is not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسری اور تیسری شرط والثانى ان يكون رب الأرض والمزارع من اهل العقد وهو لا يخص به لان عقدا ما يصح الا من الأهل والثالث بيان المدة لانه عقد على منافع الارض او منافع العامل والمدة هي المعيار لها لتعلم بها ترجمہ اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ زمین والا اور کاشتکار اہل عقد میں سے ہوں اور یہ (اہل عقد میں سے ہونا ) اسی عقد کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ کوئی عقد صحیح نہیں ہے مگر اہل ولایت سے اور شرط ثالث مدت کا بیان ہے اس لئے کہ یہ عقد زمین کے منافع پر اور مدت ہی منافع کے لئے معیار ہے تا کہ منافع کو جان لیا جائے مدت سے۔ تشریح یہ دوسری اور تیسری شرط کا بیان ہے کہ عاقدین عقد کے اہل ہونے چاہئیں مجنون وپاگل اور منی لا یعقل اس کا اہل نہیں ہوگا اور یہ اسی کی خصوصیت نہیں بلکہ ہر عقد کا یہی حال ہے کہ اس میں عاقدین اہل ولایت میں سے ہونے چاہئیں۔ نیز یہ بھی شرط ہے کہ مدت کی تعیین ہو جائے کہ عقد مزارعت کب تک کیلئے ہے جس کی دلیل متن میں مذکور ہے۔ تنبیہ غلام اور میں جبکہ ماذون ہوں تو وہ عقد مزارعت کر سکتے ہیں ہمارے دیار میں بٹائی کے لئے مدت بیان نہیں کی جاتی کیوں کہ وہ خود متعین ہے اور ایسی صورت میں تعیین مدت ضروری نہیں ہے وقيل في بلادنا تصح بلا بيان مدة ويقع على اول زرع واحد وعليه الفتوی مجتبی و بزازیه و اقره المصنف در مختار) و انما شرط محمد بيان المدة في الكوفة ونحوها لان وقتها متفاوت عندهم و ابتداؤها و انتهاؤها مجهول عند هم شامی ص ۱۸۴ ج ۵ وبعده ذکر قولاً آخر فتدبر.
Second and third condition: The second is that the landowner and the worker be among those who are eligible for the contract, and this is not specific to this contract, because no contract is valid except from the eligible. The third is the statement of the duration, because it is a contract on the usufruct of the land or the usufruct of the worker, and the duration is the measure for it, so that it may be known. Translation: The second condition is that the landowner and the worker be capable of contracting (ahl al-'aqd), and this is not specific to this contract—no contract is valid except from someone with legal capacity. The third condition is specifying the duration, because this contract involves usufruct of land or worker, and the duration is the standard for the usufruct so that it is known. Commentary: This explains the second and third conditions. The parties must be legally capable; a mad person or one with no understanding is not capable. This is not exclusive to this contract; every contract requires capable parties. Also, the duration must be determined—how long the muzara'ah is for—as the text indicates. Note: A slave and a mudabbar (one whose freedom is conditional on the master's death), when authorized, can contract muzara'ah. In our lands, for sharecropping (batai), the duration is not specified because it is self-evident (one harvest). In such a case, specifying duration is not necessary. It is said that in our country (biladuna), it is valid without mention of duration and it applies to the first crop; the fatwa is upon this. (Majtaba, Bazaziyyah, and the author of Durr Mukhtar affirmed it). Muhammad only required duration specification in Kufa and similar places because their sowing times vary and the beginning and end are unknown to them. (Shami, vol. 5, p. 184). After this, another opinion is mentioned, so consider.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage presents the second and third conditions for a valid muzara'ah contract. The second condition (sharat thani) is that both parties must be eligible to contract (ahl al-'aqd)—i.e., free, sane, mature, and with legal capacity. This is a universal requirement for all contracts. The third condition (sharat thalith) is that the duration (muddat) of the contract must be clearly stated. Since the contract is for usufruct, the duration defines the extent of usufruct. However, the Tanbih notes an exception: in our lands (probably referring to the Indian subcontinent), sharecropping (batai) is customarily for one harvest, so the duration is implicitly understood and need not be stated. This is the mufta bihi position. Imam Muhammad only required duration specification in Kufa because there the agricultural seasons were varied and uncertain. This shows the Hanafi accommodation of 'urf (custom) in making conditions flexible.

Key Terms
اہل عقد (ahl al-‘aqd): Those legally capable of entering into a contract: free, sane, mature, and discerning.
مدة (muddat): Duration of the muzara'ah contract, must be clearly expressed unless custom renders it implicit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In Hanafi muzara'ah, the duration condition is flexible when custom defines the term, and the mufta bihi does not require explicit mention.

The Fourth Condition: Specifying the Seed Provider
Fourth condition: seed provider must be specified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fourth condition of muzara'ah and explain why specifying the seed provider is essential to define the subject matter of the contract.

Core Idea
The seed provider determines whether the contract transfers land usufruct or labor usufruct.

This lesson addresses the fourth validity condition of a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract: explicitly stating who supplies the seed. The Hanafi school emphasizes this condition not as a mere formality, but as the key to identifying the ma'qud 'alayh (subject matter). Understanding this condition prevents disputes and clarifies whether the contract is essentially a lease of land or of labor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
From the text, extract the fourth condition: 'بيان من عليه البذر' (stating who bears the seed). This is a shart (condition) for validity.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The text gives two reasons: to cut off dispute (قطعاً للمنازعة) and to inform the subject matter (إعلاماً للمعقود عليه). The second reason is the core legal basis.
3
Recognize the two possibilities
The subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) is either the usufruct of the land (if worker provides seed) or the usufruct of the worker's labor (if landowner provides seed).
This dual nature is unique to muzara'ah.
4
Consequence of omission
If the seed provider is not specified, the contract is invalid because the subject matter is uncertain (gharar fahish).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوتھی شرط والرابع بيان من عليه البذر قطعا للمنازعة وإعلاماً للمعقود عليه وهو منافع الارض اومنافع العامل ترجمہ اور چوتھی شرط اس شخص کا بیان ہے جس پر پیچ ہوگا جھگڑے کو ختم کرنے کے لئے اور معقود علیہ کو بتانے کے لئے اور وہ ( معقود علیہ ) زمین کے منافع ہیں یا کاشتکار کے۔ تشریح چوتھی شرط یہ ہے کہ بیچ کون ڈالے گا اس کی تعیین ہو جائے تا کہ جھگڑ ختم ہو اور یہ معلوم ہوجائے کہ معقود علیہ کیا ہے منافع ارض ہے یا منافع عامل یعنی اگر بیج عامل کا ہو تو مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ وہ زمین کے منافع حاصل کرے گا۔ اور اگر بیج صاحب ارض کا ہو تو مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ وہ عامل کے منافع حاصل کرے گا بہر حال معقود علیہ کی تعین کے لئے بیج والے کی تصریح ہونی چاہیے۔
Fourth condition: The fourth is the statement of who bears the seed, to cut off dispute and to inform the object of the contract (ma'qud 'alayh), which is the usufruct of the land or the usufruct of the worker. Translation: The fourth condition is specifying who will provide the seed, to eliminate dispute and to clarify the object of the contract, which is either the usufruct of the land or the usufruct of the worker. Commentary: The fourth condition is that it be determined who will supply the seed, so that conflict is avoided and it becomes known what the subject matter is: the usufruct of the land or the worker. If the seed is from the worker, it means he is acquiring the usufruct of the land; if the seed is from the landowner, the landowner is acquiring the usufruct of the worker. In any case, for clarity, the seed provider must be expressly stated.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth condition (sharat rabi') for a valid muzara'ah: explicit stipulation of who provides the seed (bazr). The Arabic matn states the condition as 'بيان من عليه البذر' (stating who bears the seed). The 'illa (reason) is to prevent dispute (al-munaza'ah) and to identify the subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) of the contract. The commentary clarifies that the subject matter in muzara'ah is either the usufruct of the land (if the worker provides seed) or the usufruct of the worker's labor (if the landowner provides seed). Thus, specifying the seed provider determines the nature of the contract. For example, if the worker provides seed, the contract is essentially a lease of the land for a share of produce; if the landowner provides seed, it is a lease of the worker's labor. This precision is necessary for validity under the Sahibayn's view.

Key Terms
بذر (bazr): Seed; the provider of seed determines the nature of the muzara'ah contract.
منافع (manāfi‘): Usufruct; in muzara'ah, either the usufruct of land or the worker's labor.

Parties and Duration in Muzara'ah: Two Essential Conditions
States second and third conditions for muzara'ah validity with rational proofs and intra-Hanafi note on duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions (competent parties and specified duration) for a valid muzara'ah contract and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding duration specification.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah requires both parties to be legally competent and the duration to be known – but custom can substitute explicit duration.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah lays out two key conditions for the validity of a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract: the contracting parties must be legally competent, and the duration must be explicitly stated. However, the text also notes a significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: while Imam Muhammad required explicit duration specification in Kufa, later Hanafi jurists relaxed this condition where custom ('urf) implicitly determines the duration – and this permissive view is the relied-upon fatwa in many regions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
The text lists the second condition (both parties must be ahl al-'aqd – legally competent) and the third condition (the duration must be explicitly specified). Recognize that the first condition is the permissibility of muzara'ah itself, covered elsewhere.
Competence means sanity and majority; an authorized slave or woman is also competent.
2
Understand the rationale for duration specification
The source states that muzara'ah is a contract on benefits (manafi'), and duration is the standard (mi'yar) by which those benefits are measured. Without knowing the duration, there is ignorance (jahl) leading to gharar, which invalidates the contract.
This is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli).
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad required explicit specification of duration in all cases, but later Hanafi authorities (Majtaba, Bazaziyyah, Durr Mukhtar) and custom in certain regions relaxed this: if the custom of a single crop cycle is well-known, the duration is implicitly determined and explicit mention is not necessary.
The ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school – it is not a disagreement between madhhabs.
4
Apply the tarjih (weighting)
The mufta bihi (operative position) is the permissive view: where custom clearly indicates a single agricultural cycle, the contract is valid without specifying the duration. In Kufa or similar areas where seasons vary, Imam Muhammad's stricter view is followed.
The tarjih is based on the authority of later Hanafi masters and the principle that 'urf (custom) overrides default rules.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In a region where custom prescribes a single crop cycle, the muzara'ah contract is valid even if no duration is mentioned. In a region with variable seasons, the duration must be explicitly stated to avoid invalidity.
This shows how ikhtilaf translates into real practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(Shami vol.5 p.174). Second and third conditions: And the second is that the owner of the land and the sharecropper are among the people of contract (ahl al-aqd) – and this is not specific to this contract because no contract is valid except from the eligible. And the third is the specification of the duration because it is a contract on the benefits of the land or the benefits of the worker, and duration is the measure for them to be known. Translation: And the second condition is that the landowner and the sharecropper are among the people of contract, and this (being among the people of contract) is not specific to this contract because no contract is valid except from the people of capability. And the third condition is the specification of the duration because this contract is on the benefits of the land or the benefits of the worker, and duration is the measure for benefits so that the benefits may be known by the duration. Explanation: This is an explanation of the second and third conditions: the contracting parties must be eligible for the contract; a madman, an insane person, and one without reason are not eligible. And this is not specific to this contract; rather every contract requires the contracting parties to be from the people of capability. Also, it is a condition that the duration be specified, i.e., how long the muzara'ah contract is for, for which the proof is mentioned in the text. Note: A slave and a woman, when they are authorized, can make a muzara'ah contract. In our region, the duration is not mentioned for sharecropping because it is self-determined, and in such a case specifying the duration is not necessary. It is said that in our country it is valid without specification of duration and it applies to the first crop, and the fatwa is upon that (Majtaba and Bazaziyyah and the author affirmed in Durr Mukhtar). And Muhammad only required specification of duration in Kufa and similar places because the time is variable for them and its beginning and end are unknown to them (Shami vol.5 p.184). And after that another statement is mentioned, so ponder.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage presents the second and third conditions for the validity of a muzara'ah contract, along with an introductory note on why Imam Muhammad derived these issues from a permissive view. The second condition requires both the landowner and the worker to be legally competent (ahl al-aqd), a general requirement for all contracts. The third condition requires clear specification of the contract duration, since muzara'ah is a contract on benefits, and duration determines the extent of those benefits. The commentary then notes an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Muhammad required explicit duration specification in places like Kufa where agricultural seasons vary, but in regions where a custom (urf) determines the duration implicitly (e.g., one crop cycle), it is valid without express mention, and this is the relied-upon fatwa.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzara'ah): A contract of sharecropping where one party provides land, the other labor, and both share the produce.
اهل العقد (ahl al-'aqd): Legally competent persons (sane, adult) capable of entering a contract.
المدة (al-muddah): Duration; the period for which the muzara'ah contract is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To comply with a general requirement for all contracts.
B) Because the contract is on benefits, and duration is the measure of those benefits.
C) Because the landowner must know the exact harvest date.
D) Because the worker needs to plan his labor.

Key Takeaway
For a valid muzara'ah contract, both parties must be legally competent and the duration must be known either explicitly or by established custom, with the mufta bihi relying on the permissive view in regions with uniform seasons.

Fourth Condition of Muzara'ah: Specifying the Seed Provider
States fourth condition for muzara'ah and links it to subject matter definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fourth condition for muzara'ah and explain why specifying the seed provider is necessary to define the subject matter of the contract.

Core Idea
Seed provider determines the subject matter: if worker provides seeds, contract is on land's benefits; if landowner provides, contract is on worker's benefits.

This passage presents the fourth condition for the validity of a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract: the parties must explicitly state who will provide the seeds. This specification is not a mere formality; it determines whether the contract is over the benefits of the land or the benefits of the worker, thereby fixing the ma'qud alayh (subject matter) and eliminating future conflict. The Hanafi school insists on this condition to avoid gharar (uncertainty) and ensure the contract is properly defined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its purpose
Locate the fourth condition: specification of the seed provider. Note that its purpose is to cut off dispute (قطاعاً للمنازعة) and to inform of the subject matter (إعلاماً للمعقود عليه).
The condition is not about who actually sows, but who provides the seeds.
2
Define the subject matter of muzara'ah
Understand that the subject matter (ma'qud alayh) in muzara'ah is either the benefits of the land or the benefits of the worker, not the land or labor themselves. This distinction is crucial for the contract's nature.
Benefits (manafi') are what the contract actually conveys.
3
Link seed provision to subject matter
If the worker provides seeds, the contract is on the benefits of the land (the worker receives the crop). If the landowner provides seeds, the contract is on the benefits of the worker (the landowner receives the crop). Trace this logical connection.
The seed provider is the one who bears the primary expense for the crop.
4
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The necessity of specification is rational: without it, the subject matter is ambiguous, leading to gharar (uncertainty) which invalidates the contract. The specification ensures each party knows what they are contracting for.
Hanafi fiqh treats gharar in the subject matter as a cause for fasāḍ (voidability).
5
Note the Hanafi insistence and other schools' views
The Hanafi school considers this specification a condition (shart) for validity. Some other schools may allow seed sharing without explicit specification, but Hanafis require it to avoid dispute. Recognize this as a legitimate area of ikhtilaf.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوتھی شرط والرابع بيان من عليه البذر قطعا للمنازعة وإعلاماً للمعقود عليه وهو منافع الارض اومنافع العامل ترجمہ اور چوتھی شرط اس شخص کا بیان ہے جس پر پیچ ہوگا جھگڑے کو ختم کرنے کے لئے اور معقود علیہ کو بتانے کے لئے اور وہ ( معقود علیہ ) زمین کے منافع ہیں یا کاشتکار کے۔ تشریح چوتھی شرط یہ ہے کہ بیچ کون ڈالے گا اس کی تعیین ہو جائے تا کہ جھگڑ ختم ہو اور یہ معلوم ہوجائے کہ معقود علیہ کیاہے منافع ارض ہے یا منافع عامل یعنی اگر پیچ عامل کا ہو تو مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ وہ زمین کے منافع حاصل کرے گا۔ اور اگر پیج صاحب ارض کا ہو تو مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ وہ عامل کے منافع حاصل کر یگا بہر حال معقود علیہ کی تعین کے لئے بیج والے کی تصریح ہونی چاہیے۔
Fourth condition: And the fourth is the statement of the one upon whom the seed falls (i.e., who provides seeds) to cut off dispute and to inform of the subject matter, and it is the benefits of the land or the benefits of the worker. Translation: And the fourth condition is the specification of the person who will provide the seed in order to end dispute and to inform of the subject matter, and that (subject matter) is the benefits of the land or the benefits of the worker. Explanation: The fourth condition is that it should be specified who will sow the seed so that dispute ends and it becomes known what the subject matter is: the benefits of the land or the benefits of the worker. That is, if the seed is from the worker, it means he will receive the benefits of the land; if the seed is from the landowner, it means he will receive the benefits of the worker. In any case, for the determination of the subject matter, specification of the seed provider is necessary.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth condition for muzara'ah: the parties must specify which party provides the seeds. The reason is to avoid future disputes and to clarify the subject matter (ma'qud alayh) of the contract. In Hanafi law, the subject matter of muzara'ah is either the benefits of the land or the benefits of the worker, depending on who supplies the seeds. If the worker supplies seeds, the contract is on the benefits of the land; if the landowner supplies seeds, the contract is on the benefits of the worker. This distinction determines the nature of the compensation and the allocation of profit. Therefore, the seed provider must be expressly stated.

Key Terms
بذر (badhr): Seeds to be sown in the land for the crop.
معقود علیہ (ma'qud 'alayh): The subject matter of the contract, which in muzara'ah is either the benefits of the land or the benefits of the worker.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The worker's labor
B) The landowner's land
C) The benefits of the land
D) The seeds themselves

Key Takeaway
Specifying the seed provider is a necessary condition for the validity of muzara'ah because it defines the subject matter and prevents uncertainty.

Fifth Condition of Muzara'ah: Specifying the Non-Seed-Provider's Share
States the fifth condition and its rationale, addressing an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fifth condition of muzara'ah and explain why specifying only one share suffices according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The share of the non-seed-provider must be known because it is compensation; one specification implies the other.

Muzara'ah (sharecropping) requires several conditions to avoid uncertainty. This lesson examines the fifth condition: the share of the party who does not provide the seeds must be clearly specified. The reason is that this share is not a default right but a contractual compensation (iwad), which must be known to prevent gharar. We will also see why the Hanafis hold that specifying only one share is sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the specification of the share for the party not providing seeds in a muzara'ah contract. The ruling: it is a necessary condition (shart) for validity.
This condition is unique to the non-seed-provider; the seed-provider's share may be implied.
2
Identify the rationale (dalil aqli)
The text states: 'because he is entitled to it as compensation by the condition, so it must be known.' The legal reasoning: this share is an iwad (compensation), and in Hanafi contract law, iwad must be known to avoid gharar. Therefore, the share must be specified.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the nature of contractual compensation.
3
Consider the objection
The author of Nata'ij al-Afkar objected: why is specification of only one share (the seed-provider's share) considered sufficient? According to the objector, both shares should be explicitly specified.
This objection represents a divergent view within Hanafi scholarship.
4
Apply the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position is that specifying the seed-provider's share suffices because it logically implies the remainder belongs to the non-seed-provider. The contract is valid without explicit statement of both shares.
The principle: if one share is known, the other is determined by subtraction from the whole.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that specification of one share is sufficient; the other is implied. Therefore, the objection is not upheld.
This is the mufta bihi and is based on the rational inference of contractual terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پانچویں شرط والخامس بيان نصيب من لا بذر من قبله لانه يستحقه عوضا بالشرط فلا بدان يكون معلوما وما لا يعلم لا يستحق شرطا بالعقد ترجمہ اور پانچواں شرط اس شخص کے حصہ کا بیان ہے جس کی جانب پیچ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ مستحق ہوتا ہے اس کا بطور عوض کے شرط کی وجہ سے پس ضروری ہے کہ وہ معلوم ہو اور جس چیز کو جانا نہیں جائیگا تو اس کا استحقاق عقد کی وجہ سے شرط بن کر ہو گا۔ تشریح جس کا بیج نہیں ہے اس کا حصہ متعین ہونا چاہیے اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے حصہ کا مستحق شرط کی وجہ سے ہی ہوتا ہے تو اس کا حصہ متعین ہونا ضروری ہے ورنہ اگر حصہ معلوم نہ ہوگا تو پھر شرط کی وجہ سے استحقاق کیسے ثابت ہوگا۔ اگر بیچ والے کا حصہ متعین ہو جائے اور دوسرے کے حصہ سے سکوت ہو تب بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ خود اس کو واضح کر دے گا کہ دوسرے کا حصہ اتنا ہوگا۔ لہذا صاحب نتائج الافکار کا اعتراض کوئی حیثیت نہیں رکے گا کہ ایک کی تعیین ہی کیوں شرط ہے۔
Fifth condition: And the fifth is the specification of the share of the one from whose side the seed is not, because he is entitled to it as compensation by the condition, so it must be known; and what is not known cannot be entitled as a condition in the contract. Translation: And the fifth condition is the specification of the share of the person who does not provide the seed, because he is entitled to it as compensation by virtue of the condition, so it is necessary that it be known; and that which is not known cannot be entitled as a condition in the contract. Explanation: The share of the one who does not have seeds must be specified because he is only entitled to his share by reason of the condition; therefore his share must be specified, otherwise if the share is unknown, how can entitlement be established through the condition? If the share of the seed provider is specified and the other's share is silent, it is still valid because it makes clear that the other's share will be the remainder. Therefore, the objection of the author of Nata'ij al-Afkar has no standing that specifying only one share is not sufficient.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth condition for muzara'ah: the share of the party who does not provide seeds must be clearly specified. The reasoning is that this share is not a natural right but a contractual compensation (iwad) fixed by mutual condition. Since the contract establishes entitlement through the condition, the share must be known to avoid gharar (uncertainty). The commentary notes a subtle point: if the seed provider's share is specified and the other's share is left unstated, the contract is still valid because it implies the remaining share belongs to the other party. This counters an objection raised by the author of Nata'ij al-Afkar, who questioned why only one share needs specification. The Hanafi position is that specification of one share suffices when the remainder is clear by inference.

Key Terms
عوض (iwad): Compensation or consideration in a contract; here the share is a substitute for the non-seed-provider's contribution.
شرط (shart): A condition stipulated in the contract that creates entitlement to the share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why must the share of the party not providing seeds be specified?
A) Because it is a condition in the contract that cannot be defaulted
B) Because he is entitled to it as compensation by condition, so it must be known
C) Because the seed provider's share is always fixed by default
D) Because the landowner's share must be declared first

Key Takeaway
The share of the non-seed-provider must be known, but specifying the other share implies it, making the contract valid without explicit dual specification.

Three Conditions for Valid Muzara'ah: Takhliyah, Partnership, and Seed Specification
Lists three conditions for muzara'ah validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for a valid muzara'ah contract and explain why each is necessary for validity.

Core Idea
A muzara'ah contract is invalid if the landowner retains control, the produce is not shared, or the seed type is unspecified.

The Hanafi school sets precise conditions for the validity of a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract. This lesson covers three essential conditions: the landowner must vacate the land (takhliyah), the produce must be jointly owned (shirkah), and the type of seed must be specified. Violating any of these makes the contract fasid (invalid). Understanding these conditions distinguishes a valid Islamic partnership from a potentially exploitative arrangement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
List the three conditions mentioned in the passage: (1) landowner vacates the land, (2) produce is shared as partnership, (3) seed type is specified. Note the order.
Conditions 6, 7, and 8 are presented sequentially.
2
Analyze the rationale for takhliyah
The landowner must have no involvement in the work. If he stipulates his own labor, his involvement persists, destroying the nature of the contract as a pure partnership between land and labor.
Takhliyah ensures the worker has full control over cultivation.
3
Analyze the rationale for shirkah
Muzara'ah is a partnership in the final produce. Any condition that fixes a specific quantity for one party (e.g., 10 mann for the landowner) undermines joint ownership, as the actual yield may be less.
This condition prevents gharar (uncertainty) and ensures the partnership is genuine.
4
Analyze the rationale for seed specification
The seed type affects the anticipated yield and therefore the 'wage' (ajr) of the worker. Specifying it removes ambiguity about the worker’s compensation.
Without specification, the wage is unknown, leading to potential dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چھٹی شرط والسادس ان يخلى رب الأرض بينهما وبين العامل حتى لو شرط عمل رب الأرض يفسد العقد لفوات التخلية والسابع الشركة فى الخارج بعد حصوله لانه ينعقد شركة فى الانتهاء فما يقطع هذه الشركة كان مفسد العقد والثامن بيا س البذر ليصير الاجر معلوما ترجمہ اور چھٹی شرط یہ ہے کہ زمین والا زمین اور عامل کے درمیان تخلیہ کر دے یہاں تک کہ اگر زمین والے کے کام کی شرط لگائی گئی تو عقد فاسد ہو جائے گا تخلیہ کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ساتھ میں شرط پیداوار میں شرکت ہے پیداوار میں حاصل ہونے کے بعد اس لئے کہ یہ عقد شرکت بن کر منعقد ہوتا ہے انتہاء میں تو جو شرط اس شرکت کو ختم کر دے وہ مفسد عقد ہوگی اور آٹھویں شرط پیج کے جنس کو بیان کرنا ہے تا کہ اجرت معلوم ہو جائے۔ تشریح چھٹی شرط یہ ہے کہ زمین میں مالک زمین کا کوئی دخل نہ رہے ( بیج خواہ مالک کا ہو یا کاشتکار کا۔ اور ہر وہ شرط جو زمین کے دخل کوختم نہ کر سکے وہ مفید عقد ہوگی۔ لہذا اگر زمین والے پر کام کی شرط ہو گی تو اس کا دخل برقرار ہے لہذ ا عقد فاسد ہوگا۔ اور اگر زمین میں کھیتی اگ گئی ہو اور اس وقت عامل کے حوالہ کی گئی تو یہ معاملہ ہے مزارعت نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر کھیتی تیار ہو گئی تو چونکہ اب اس میں عامل کے عمل کی ضرورت نہیں رہی اب اس کو معاملہ بنا کر بھی جائز کہنا دشوار ہو گیا۔ شامی ص ۱۷۵ ج ۵ ساتھ میں شرط . پیداوار میں دونوں کا شریک ہونا تو جو شرط اس شرکت کو ختم کرے وہ مفسد عقد ہو گی مثلا پیداوار میں سے ایک کا دس من باقی مشترک تو شرکت ختم ہوگئی کیوں کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ پیداوار اتنی ہی ہو یا اتنی بھی نہ ہو ( وسیاتی تفصیلہ )
Sixth condition: And the sixth is that the landowner vacates (the land) between himself and the worker, such that if he stipulates the work of the landowner, the contract is invalid due to loss of vacation. And the seventh is the partnership in the produce after its occurrence, because the contract is concluded as a partnership in the end, so whatever cuts this partnership is a corruptor of the contract. And the eighth is the specification of the type of seed so that the wage becomes known. Translation: The sixth condition is that the landowner should vacate between the land and the worker, so much so that if the landowner's work is stipulated, the contract becomes invalid due to the loss of vacation. And along with that, the condition is partnership in the produce after it is obtained, because this contract is concluded as a partnership in the end, so any condition that cuts this partnership is a corruptor of the contract. And the eighth condition is to specify the type of seed so that the wage becomes known. Explanation: The sixth condition is that the landowner should have no involvement in the land (whether seed is from owner or worker). And any condition that does not remove the landowner's involvement will invalidate the contract. Therefore, if the landowner stipulates work for himself, his involvement remains, so the contract is invalid. And if the crop has already grown and then handed over to the worker, this is a transaction (mu'amalah), not muzara'ah. And if the crop is ready, since the worker's labor is no longer needed, it becomes difficult to consider it valid even as a mu'amalah. (Shami vol.5 p.175). Along with the condition of partnership in produce: so any condition that ends this partnership is a corruptor, e.g., specifying a fixed amount (e.g., 10 mann) for one party from the produce while the rest is shared – then partnership ends because the produce might be exactly that amount or less. (Details will come).
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents three final conditions for muzara'ah. The sixth condition requires the landowner to vacate (takhliyah) the land, meaning he must not retain any control or involvement. If he stipulates his own work, the contract becomes invalid because his involvement persists. The seventh condition requires that the produce be shared between both parties, as muzara'ah is fundamentally a partnership in the outcome. Any condition that undermines this joint ownership (e.g., fixing a specific quantity for one party regardless of actual yield) invalidates the contract. The eighth condition requires specification of the seed type so that the 'wage' (ajr) – i.e., the share of produce as compensation – is known, since the seed type affects the anticipated yield and value. The commentary further clarifies that if the crop is already grown before contracting, it is not muzara'ah but a different transaction (mu'amalah).

Key Terms
تخلیہ (takhliyah): The landowner vacating the land, i.e., not retaining any control or work involvement.
شركة (shirkah): Partnership; here meaning joint ownership of the produce after harvest.
اجرت (ujrat (ajr)): Wage; here the share of the worker (or landowner) as compensation for their contribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following would invalidate a muzara'ah contract according to the eighth condition (seed specification)?
A) Stipulating that worker provides seeds
B) Stipulating that landowner does some work on the land
C) Specifying the type of seed to be used
D) Leaving the seed type unspecified

Key Takeaway
The validity of a muzara'ah contract hinges on three conditions: landowner vacates, produce is shared, and seed type is specified; violating any makes the contract invalid.

Conditions Five to Eight for a Valid Muzara'ah Contract
Listing four conditions for valid muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fifth through eighth conditions of a valid muzara'ah contract and explain why each is necessary for validity.

Core Idea
A muzara'ah contract requires known shares, landowner non-interference, partnership in produce, and specified seed type.

The passage enumerates four key conditions that ensure clarity and fairness in a sharecropping arrangement. Understanding these conditions prevents common invalidating stipulations. Each condition addresses a potential source of gharar (uncertainty) or injustice, making the contract sound in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Fifth Condition
The share of the party who does not provide the seed must be clearly known at the time of contracting. This is because that share is the worker's compensation, and compensation must be known to avoid gharar.
If the worker's share is specified, the landowner's share is implied as the remainder; this suffices.
2
Identify the Sixth Condition
The landowner must fully relinquish control of the land to the worker (takhliyah). If the landowner stipulates any work for himself, the contract is void because the worker's exclusive access is lost.
Takhliyah means leaving the land free for the worker's exclusive use.
3
Identify the Seventh Condition
The contract must create a genuine partnership (shirkah) in the produce after it is harvested. Any stipulation that gives a fixed amount to one party or otherwise negates this partnership invalidates the contract.
The essence of muzara'ah is sharing the final yield proportionally.
4
Identify the Eighth Condition
The type of seed (or crop) to be sown must be specified. This makes the worker's wage (the share) known in genus, and also informs the landowner how the land will be used.
If the seed type is left unknown, the contract suffers from gharar and is void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخامس بيان نصيب من لا بذر من قبله لانه يستحقه عوضا بالشرط فلا بدان يكون معلوما وما لا يعلم لا يستحق شرطا بالعقد
والسادس ان يخلى رب الأرض بينهما وبين العامل حتى لو شرط عمل رب الأرض يفسد العقد لفوات التخلية والسابع الشركة فى الخارج بعد حصوله لانه ينعقد شركة فى الانتهاء فما يقطع هذه الشركة كان مفسد العقد والثامن بيا س البذر ليصير الاجر معلوما
(تشريح: جس کا بیج نہیں ہے اس کا حصہ متعین ہونا چاہیے... اور آٹھویں شرط یہ ہے کہ یہ متعین ہو جائے کہ زمین میں کیا بویا جائے گا۔)
And the fifth condition: clarification of the share of the one with no seed from him, because he is entitled to it as a compensation by the condition, so it must be known; and what is not known cannot be entitled as a condition by the contract. And the sixth condition: that the owner of the land leaves (the land) between him (the owner) and the worker; even if he stipulates the work of the owner of the land, the contract becomes void due to the loss of leaving (free access). And the seventh: partnership in the produce after its acquisition, because the contract is concluded as a partnership in the end; so anything that eliminates this partnership is a corruptor of the contract. And the eighth: making known the type of seed so that the wage becomes known. (Commentary: The share of the one with no seed must be specified... And the eighth condition is that it becomes specified what will be sown in the land.)
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage enumerates the fifth through eighth conditions for the validity of a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract according to the Hanafi school. The fifth condition requires that the share of the party who does not provide the seed (usually the worker) be known and definite at the time of contract. This is because that share is his compensation for work, and compensation must be known to avoid gharar. If the worker's share is specified but the other's share remains silent, it is still valid because the remainder can be deduced. The sixth condition is that the landowner must relinquish control of the land to the worker fully; if the landowner stipulates any work for himself, the contract is void because the worker lacks full access. The seventh condition is that the contract creates a partnership in the produce, so any stipulation that nullifies this partnership (e.g., allocating a fixed amount to one party) invalidates the contract. The eighth condition requires specifying the type of seed (or plant) to be sown, because the produce is the wage, and its genus must be known; also different plants affect the land differently, so the landowner's consent depends on that. These conditions ensure fairness and clarity.

Key Terms
تخلیہ (takhliyah): Leaving the land free for the worker's exclusive access and work.
شرکہ فی الخارج (shirkah fi al-kharij): Partnership in the produce after it comes into existence.
بيان البذر (bayan al-budhr): Specifying the type of seed or crop to be sown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Sixth condition: takhliyah of the land.
C) Seventh condition: partnership in produce.
D) Eighth condition: specifying the type of seed.

Key Takeaway
The validity of muzara'ah hinges on known shares, exclusive worker access, genuine partnership in produce, and specific seed type.

First Two Forms of Muzara'ah According to the Sahibayn
Explaining the first two of four permissible forms of muzara'ah as held by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first two forms of muzara'ah approved by the Sahibayn and apply the analogy to ijarah to validate them.

Core Idea
The Sahibayn validate muzara'ah by analogizing to ijarah: land leased for a share of the crop is like renting land for cash.

This passage expands the permissible forms of muzara'ah beyond Imam Abu Hanifa's stricter conditions. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) introduce two additional valid structures by analogizing to ijarah—hiring a tailor or leasing land. Understanding their reasoning helps you grasp how analogical extension works within the Hanafi school and why their view became the operative position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two forms
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Form 1: land and seed from one party, ox and work from the other. Form 2: land from one party, all else (work, ox, seed) from the other.
These are two of four total forms according to Sahibayn.
2
Understand the analogy for each form
For Form 1, the ox is classified as a tool (ālah al-ʿamal), analogous to a tailor's needle. Thus the arrangement is like hiring a tailor who uses his own needle. For Form 2, it is a straight lease of land for a known share of produce, analogous to leasing land for known dirhams.
The qiyas (analogy) is the key proof (dalīl ʿaqlī).
3
Recognize the intra-madhhab dispute
The Sahibayn's position expands the validity of muzara'ah. Imam Abu Hanifa had stricter requirements—he only allowed muzara'ah when land, seed, ox, and labor are split in a specific manner. The Sahibayn's view is more facilitative.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf resolved in favor of the Sahibayn.
4
Determine the operative ruling
Later Hanafi scholars (e.g., in al-Hidayah) accept the Sahibayn's view as the muftā bihī (operative for fatwa). Thus both forms are valid and enforceable.
Authority weight: Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وهى عندهما على اربعة أوجه وان كانت الارض والبذر لو احد والبقر والعمل لواحد جازت المزراعة لان البقرآلة العمل فصار كما اذا استاجر خياطا ليخيط بابرة الخياط
وان كان الأرض لو احد والعمل والبقر والبذر لواحد جازت لانه استيجار الأرض ببعض معلوم من الخارج فيجوز كما اذا استاجرها بدراهم معلومة
He said: And it (muzara'ah) according to them (the Sahibayn) is of four forms: (First:) If the land and seed belong to one party, and the ox and work belong to one party, then muzara'ah is valid, because the ox is a tool of work; so it is as if he hired a tailor to sew with the tailor's needle. (Second:) And if the land belongs to one, and the work, ox, and seed belong to one, it is valid, because it is a lease of the land for a known portion of the produce; thus it is permissible, like if he leased it for known dirhams.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents the first two of four forms of muzara'ah that are valid according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The first form: one party provides land and seed, the other provides ox and labor. The ox is considered a tool (like a needle for a tailor), so the contract is analogous to hiring a worker with his own tool. The second form: one party provides only land, the other provides labor, ox, and seed. This is a straightforward lease of land for a share of the produce, analogous to leasing land for a fixed cash rent. Both forms are valid because the compensation (share) is known and the arrangement resembles a valid ijarah. The Sahibayn's view is more expansive than Imam Abu Hanifa's original strictness, and it is the relied-upon position in the school.

Key Terms
آلة العمل (ālah al-ʿamal): Tool of work; here the ox is considered a tool analogous to a tailor's needle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The party who also provides the land.
B) The party who provides the ox and work.
C) A third party not involved in land or work.
D) Both parties jointly.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's expansion of muzara'ah through qiyas makes the contract valid in two additional forms, which are now the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.

Invalidity of Muzara'ah with Rented Bullocks
Analysis of an invalid form of muzara'ah using four principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a muzara'ah contract where the worker rents both land and bullocks for a share of the produce, explain the four principles that lead to its invalidity, and apply the rule that subordination (tab‘iyyah) requires unity of kind (ittihad al-jins).

Core Idea
Muzara'ah is a restricted permission: land can be rented for a share, not bullocks; land and bullocks are different kinds and cannot be subordinated.

The Hanafi school permits certain forms of muzara'ah (sharecropping) by explicit textual proof (nas), but strictly limits them to those forms. This passage analyzes a specific invalid form where the worker rents both land and bullocks for a share of the produce. The author lays down four foundational principles and uses them to demonstrate why this contract is invalid, emphasizing the limits of analogy (qiyas) and the requirement of unity of kind for subordination (tab‘iyyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is a muzara'ah contract where the 'amil (worker) rents both land and bullocks in exchange for a share of the produce. The ruling is that such a contract is fasid (invalid/defective).
The passage uses 'fasid' (فاسد) to indicate invalidity.
2
Trace the four foundational principles
The author lists four principles before analyzing the case. Memorize them: (1) Muzara'ah begins as ijarah (hire) and ends as shirkah (partnership). (2) Anything established contrary to qiyas by nas is confined to that specific case and cannot be extended by qiyas. (3) Renting land for a known share of produce is permissible; renting bullocks for a share is not. (4) Subordination (tab‘iyyah) requires unity of kind (ittihad al-jins).
These principles are the legal framework for this ruling.
3
Apply the principles to the case
Using principle 3, the rental of bullocks for a share of produce is directly impermissible. Even if one argues that the bullocks are subordinate to the land (principle 4), the attempt fails because the benefits of land and bullocks are of different kinds: land provides 'establishment' (e.g., growth) while bullocks provide physical effort (ploughing). Thus, subordination is invalid.
4
Analyze the objection and response
An objector might claim that the bullocks are subordinate to the land. The author refutes this by explaining that subordination requires unity of kind, which is absent here. The difference in jins is proven by the difference in the nature of the benefits.
Note the precision: the benefit of land is static and growth-oriented; the benefit of bullocks is kinetic and labour-oriented.
5
Understand the role of nas and qiyas
The author notes that general qiyas would prohibit all muzara'ah, but the Shariah allowed specific forms via nas. This particular case is not covered by that nas, so it returns to the general qiyas and is declared invalid. This reinforces the principle that exceptional permissions cannot be extended by analogy.
Key takeaway: The boundaries of a textual concession are fixed; one cannot analogize beyond them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یہاں اولا چار باتیں ذہن میں رکھئے۔
- مزارعت شروع میں عقد اجارہ ہے اور انتہاء کے اعتبار سے شرکت ہے۔
جو چیز خلاف قیاس ہوتی ہے وہ مورد شرع تک رہتی ہے دوسرے کو اس پر قیاس نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔
پیداوار کے معلوم حصہ کے بدلہ زمین کرایہ پر لینا جائز ہے بیلوں کو اجارہ پر لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔

كتاب المزارعة .
تو اب سنئے کہ صورت مذکورہ میں شرکت کا انعقاد نہیں ہوا اسلئے کہ شرکت کا انعقاد بیل اور عامل کی منفعت کے درمیان نہیں ہوتا حالانکہ مزارعت باعتبار انتہاء شرکت ہے اسلئے یہ صورت فاسد ہے۔

نہیں ہے کہ بیلوں کو کرایہ پر لیا جائے اور اجرت پیداوار کا کچھ حصہ ہو اسلئے یہ صورت جائز نہیں ہوگی۔
اعتراض اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ عامل نے زمین کرایہ پر لی ہے اور بیل زمین کے تابع ہیں؟
جواب تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بیل عامل کے تابع تو ہو سکے نہیں زمین کے تابع نہیں ہوں گے اسلئے کہ تبعیت کیلئے اتحاد جنس چاہئے اور منافع ارض اور منافع بقر میں اختلاف جنس ہے۔ کیونکہ ایک کی منفعت اثبات اور دوسرے کی شق اور پھاڑنا ہے پھر ایک کی منفعت قوت حیوانیہ کی وجہ سے ہے اور زمین کی اور وجہ سے ہے۔
اسلئے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ دونوں مختلف الجنس ہیں جس میں تبعیت نہیں ہو سکتی اور جب نہیں سکتی تو شرکت بالبقر ہوئی اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ نیز قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ تھا کہ مزارعت جائز نہ ہو مگر ہم نے نص کی وجہ سے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا اور نص کے او پر عمل کیا لیکن مورد نص وہ دیگر صورتیں ہیں یہ صورت مورد نص نہیں ہے اسلئے حسب قاعدہ مسلمہ اس کو نا جائز کہا جائے گا کیونکہ دیگر صورتوں پر اس کو قیاس نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔
Here, first keep four things in mind. 1. Muzara'ah is initially a contract of hire (ijarah) and in terms of its end it is a partnership (shirkah). 2. Something that is contrary to analogy (qiyas) remains confined to the place of the text (nas) and cannot be analogized to others. 3. Renting land for a known share of the produce is permissible; renting bullocks on hire is not permissible. 4. Two things of different kinds cannot be made subordinate to each other; subordination (tab'iyyah) is permissible in case of difference of kind. When these things are understood. Kitab al-Muzara'ah. Now listen: in the mentioned case, partnership did not occur because partnership does not occur between the bullock and the worker's benefit, even though muzara'ah by its end is a partnership, so this case is defective (fasid). Also, the worker has rented the land and the bullocks, and both are intended to be rented, and the wage is a part of the produce. And it is not permissible for bullocks to be rented and the wage be a part of the produce, so this case will not be permissible. Objection: If it is objected that the worker rented the land and the bullocks are subordinate to the land? Answer: The response is that the bullocks cannot be subordinate to the worker, nor will they be subordinate to the land, because subordination requires unity of kind (ittihad al-jins), and there is difference of kind between the benefit of land and the benefit of bullocks. Because the benefit of one is [tilling/establishment?] and the benefit of the other is splitting and tearing. Also, the benefit of one is due to animal power, and that of the land is due to another cause. So it is understood that these two are of different kinds, in which subordination cannot occur, and when it cannot, then it becomes a partnership in bullocks (shirkat al-baqar), and this is not permissible. Also, the requirement of analogy (qiyas) was that muzara'ah would not be permissible, but we left qiyas due to the text (nas) and acted upon the text. However, the application of the text is other cases; this case is not the subject of the text. Therefore, according to the established principle, it should be declared impermissible, because other cases cannot be analogized to it.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on an invalid form of muzara'ah (sharecropping). The author first lays down four foundational principles: (1) Muzara'ah begins as an ijarah (hire) contract for the land but ends as a shirkah (partnership) in the produce. (2) Something established by a textual proof (nas) that contradicts qiyas (analogy) is restricted to that specific case and cannot be extended by qiyas to other cases. (3) It is permissible to rent land for a share of produce, but it is not permissible to rent bullocks for a share of produce. (4) Subordination (tab'iyyah) is allowed only when the two things are of the same type; if they are of different types, subordination is not valid. Using these principles, the author analyzes a specific case where the worker (amil) rents both land and bullocks in exchange for a share of the produce. This is invalid for two reasons: first, the bullocks are being rented for a share of produce, which is explicitly impermissible (principle 3). Second, even if one argues that the bullocks are subordinate to the land, this fails because the benefits of land and bullocks are of different kinds (principle 4): land provides 'establishment' (perhaps growth) while bullocks provide physical effort like ploughing. The author then addresses an objection: perhaps the bullocks are subordinate to the land. The response is that subordination requires unity of kind (ittihad al-jins), which is absent here. Therefore, this case results in a partnership in the bullocks themselves, which is not a valid form of muzara'ah. Finally, the author invokes the principle that while general qiyas would have prohibited all muzara'ah, the Shariah allowed certain specific forms by nas. This particular form is not among those allowed by nas, so it returns to the general qiyas and is declared invalid. The lesson emphasizes that one cannot extend the permission of nas by analogy to other forms.

Key Terms
مزارعت (muzāra‘ah): A contract for sharecropping where one party provides land and the other works it, sharing the produce.
تبعیت (tab‘iyyah): Subordination: one thing being considered legally dependent on another, allowed only when both are of the same type.
اختلاف جنس (ikhtilāf al-jins): Difference in kind or category between two items, preventing legal subordination.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.
نص (naṣṣ): Explicit textual proof from Quran or Sunnah that establishes a ruling directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the form of muzara'ah where the worker rents both land and bullocks for a share of produce invalid according to this passage?
A) Because both the land and bullocks are rented, which is not allowed.
B) Because the bullocks cannot be rented for a share of produce, and they are not subordinate to the land due to difference in kind.
C) Because the worker does not own the bullocks.
D) Because the contract becomes a partnership in bullocks, which is valid only if the bullocks are owned by both parties.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, muzara'ah is permitted only in specific forms by textual proof; including bullocks in the rental for a share is invalid, and they cannot be subordinated to land due to difference in kind.

Fifth and Sixth Invalid Forms of Muzara'ah
Expansion of invalid forms by analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas principle to identify invalid forms of muzara'ah based on the prohibition of partnership between seed and labor or seed and bullocks.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah cannot be a partnership in seed; any contract structured as such is batil.

Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar lists four invalid forms of muzara'ah, but the later Hanafi masters identify two more. These arise when the contract creates an impermissible partnership between seed and labor or between seed and bullocks. In this lesson, we explore the reasoning behind these rulings and how qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) establishes their invalidity.

Guided Path
1
State the two new forms
Identify each form: (1) seed belongs to one party, everything else to the other; (2) seed and bullocks together belong to one party, land and labor to the other.
These are extensions of the principle that seed must be jointly owned or mixed.
2
Identify the ruling
Both forms are ruled batil (void). The text says 'la yajuz' (not permissible).
Batil means the contract has no legal effect; no returns are due.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause)
The common element in both is that seed is entirely owned by one party, creating a shirkah (partnership) between seed and something else (labor or bullocks) unsanctioned by Shariah.
Valid muzara'ah requires joint ownership of seed (or at least mixed ownership).
4
Apply qiyas jaliy
Since the asl (original case) is any form where seed is on one side alone (already known invalid), the far' (new case) includes the combination of seed+bullocks on one side, which is a fortiori invalid.
Qiyas jaliy: the far' shares the same illa as the asl.
5
Confirm the thamarah (practical consequence)
The contract is void; no share of crop is due to the laborer. The produce belongs entirely to the owner of the land and seed (if both are same) or to the owner of the seed (if landowner provides seed).
This differs from valid muzara'ah where both parties share produce.

Source Text

چھٹی صورت
والثانى ان يجمع بين البذر والبقر وانه لا يجوز ايضا لانه لا يجوز عند الانفراد فكذا عند الاجتماع
ترجمہ اور دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ بیج اور بیل کے درمیان جمع کر دیا جائے اور یہ بھی جائز نہیں تو اسلئے کہ یہ انفراد کے وقت جائز نہیں تو ایسے ہی اجتماع کے وقت۔

Fifth form: 'And here are two other aspects that he did not mention. One is that the seed belongs to one of them, and the land, bullocks, and work belong to the other, and it is not permissible because it would be a partnership between seed and labor, and the Shariah did not come with it.' Translation: And here are two more forms that al-Quduri did not mention. Among them, one is that the seed belongs to one of them, and the land, bullocks, and work belong to the other, and this is not permissible because this contract becomes a partnership between seed and labor, whereas the Shariah has not come with it. Explanation: This is the fifth form that al-Quduri did not mention: if Zayd's seed and the rest belong to 'Amr, this is also invalid. Sixth form: 'And the second is that one combines seed and bullocks, and it is also not permissible, because it is not permissible in isolation, so likewise in combination.' Translation: And the second form is that seed and bullocks are combined, and this is also not permissible, because it is not permissible individually, so likewise when combined. Explanation: This is the sixth form: if Zayd has bullocks and seed, and 'Amr provides land and work, this form is also invalid. Because if only seed is on one side and everything else on the other, it is not permissible. Also, if bullocks are on one side and everything else on the other, it is not permissible. In this case, both (seed and bullocks) are combined, and what is invalid individually will also be invalid in combination.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents two additional invalid forms of muzara'ah that were not mentioned by al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar. The first additional form (fifth overall) is when one party provides only the seed, and the other party provides the land, bullocks, and labor. This is invalid because it creates a partnership between seed and labor only, which is not a form of muzara'ah recognized by the Shariah. The second additional form (sixth overall) is when one party provides both seed and bullocks, and the other provides land and labor. This is also invalid because each element individually (seed on one side, bullocks on the other) is already invalid in isolation, so combining them does not make it valid. The principle is that muzara'ah must be structured in a way that is sanctioned by the revealed texts; any deviation that introduces elements not covered by the nas (like direct partnership between seed and labor, or combining impermissible elements) renders the contract batil (void). The author emphasizes that Quduri's enumeration was not exhaustive, but these additional forms follow the same legal reasoning.

Key Terms
بذر (badhr): Seed grain used in agriculture.
شركة (shirkah): Partnership; in this context, an unauthorized partnership between seed and labor or seed and bullocks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sixth invalid form of muzara'ah, why is the contract invalid even though the parties have contributed different items?
A) Because the seed is not owned by the landowner.
B) Because it combines two elements (seed and bullocks) that are each individually impermissible in such contracts.
C) Because the labor is not compensated.
D) Because the contract is a partnership in bullocks, which is not allowed.

Key Takeaway
Muzara'ah contracts that place seed entirely on one side (whether alone or with other contributions) are batil because they create an impermissible shirkah in seed.

Ruling on Produce in Invalid Muzara'ah
Determination of who gets the produce in invalid forms of muzara'ah based on two narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations on produce ownership in invalid muzara'ah and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
In invalid muzara'ah, the produce belongs to the seed owner – the second narration is not relied upon in later Hanafi texts.

When a muzara'ah contract is fasid (invalid), the key question is: who owns the produce? The Hanafi school contains two early narrations with different conclusions. This lesson unpacks both, showing how later authorities weighed them and standardized the ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the two narratives
Identify the two transmitted rulings (riwayat) regarding produce ownership in invalid muzara'ah as presented in Al-Hidayah.
Focus on the seed owner vs land owner distinction.
2
Examine the evidence for each narration
For the first narration: analogy (qiyas) to all other invalid muzara'ah contracts. For the second: the land owner takes possession of the seed by its attachment to his land, making him a borrower (mustaqrid).
The loan construct is a legal device to explain ownership transfer.
3
Understand the objection and response
A loan requires possession (qabd). How is the land owner considered in possession? By the seed's attachment to his land, which constitutes constructive possession (qabd hukmi).
This is a key Hanafi concept.
4
Evaluate the later Hanafi tarjih
The commentator notes that the second narration is not found in later authoritative works like Durr al-Mukhtar, Bada'i', and Majma' al-Anhur. The first narration (produce for seed owner) is the mufta bihi.
This shows how intra-madhhab disputes are resolved over time.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the mufta bihi, the seed owner gets the produce; according to the weaker narration, the land owner gets it but must repay the seed value.
In fatwa, the first position is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخارج فى الوجهين لصاحب البذر فى رواية اعتباراً بسائر المزارعات الفاسدة وفي رواية لصاحب الارض ويصير مستقرضا للبذر قابضـه باتصـالـه بــارضه
ترجمہ اور پیداوار دونوں صورتوں میں ایک روایت کے مطابق بیج والے کی ہوگی۔ تمام مزارعات فاسدہ پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور ایک روایت کے مطابق زمین والے کی اور ہو جائے گا وہ بیج کو قرض لینے والا در آنحالیکہ وہ بیج پر قبضہ کرنے والا ہو گا بیج کے متصل ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی زمین کے ساتھ۔ 
تشریح جن صورتوں کے اندر مزارعت فاسد ہے ان میں پیداوار کس کی ہوگی تو صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ پہلی روایت یہ ہے کہ جس کا بیج ہو گا اس کی پیداوار ہو گی۔ اسلئے کہ مزارعات فاسدہ کی تمام صورتوں میں یہی حکم ہے تو یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہوگا۔
اور دوسری راویت یہ ہے کہ پیداوار زمین والے کی ہوگی اور زمین والے نے بیج والے سے بیج قرض لیا ہے۔
سوال قرض کیلئے ضروری ہے کہ قرض لینے والا اس پر قبضہ کرے اور یہاں قبضہ ندارد ہے۔
جواب جب بیج زمین والے کی زمین سے متصل ہو گیا تو یہ صاحب ارض کا قبضہ ہو گیا ہے۔ ان دونوں روایتوں کو صدر الشہید نے ذکر کیا ہے۔
قلت شامی، درمختار بدائع مجمع الانہر وغیرہ میں دوسری روایت نہیں ملی بلکہ تمام کتب کے اندر یہ حکم بیان کیا گیا ہے کہ مزارعت فاسدہ میں پیداوار صاحب بذر کی ہوگی۔
And the produce in the two aspects (forms): according to one narration it belongs to the owner of the seed, by analogy to all invalid muzara'ah contracts; and in another narration it belongs to the owner of the land, and he becomes a borrower of the seed, having taken possession of it by its attachment to his land. Translation: And the produce in both forms: according to one narration it will be for the seed owner, by analogy to all invalid muzara'ah contracts; and according to another narration it will be for the land owner, and he becomes a borrower of the seed, while he is in possession of the seed due to its attachment to his land. Explanation: In the forms where muzara'ah is invalid, who will get the produce? The author of Al-Hidayah said there are two narrations. The first narration is that the one who owns the seed will get the produce, because this is the ruling in all invalid muzara'ah contracts, so here it will be the same. The second narration is that the produce will be for the land owner, and the land owner borrowed the seed from the seed owner. Question: For a loan, it is necessary that the borrower take possession, and here there is no possession. Answer: When the seed becomes attached to the land owner's land, that constitutes possession by the land owner. These two narrations were mentioned by Sadr al-Shahid. I say: In Shami, Durr al-Mukhtar, Bada'i', Majma' al-Anhur, etc., I did not find the second narration; rather, in all books it is stated that in invalid muzara'ah, the produce belongs to the seed owner.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage deals with the consequence of an invalid muzara'ah contract: who owns the produce? The author presents two narrations from the Hanafi school. The first, which is more widely accepted, states that the produce belongs to the owner of the seed. This is by analogy (qiyas) to all other cases of invalid muzara'ah where the seed owner is considered the owner of the produce. The second narration, mentioned by Sadr al-Shahid (a Hanafi jurist), says the produce belongs to the land owner, but the land owner is deemed to have borrowed the seed from the seed owner, and he must return its value. This second view is based on the idea that the seed, once planted, becomes part of the land and is thus possessed by the land owner, making him a borrower. The author (the commentator) then notes that in later authoritative works like al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Bada'i' al-Sana'i', and Majma' al-Anhur, the second narration is not found; instead, all these books state the first ruling: the produce is for the seed owner. This indicates that the first narration is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the later Hanafi school. The objection about possession for the loan is answered: attachment to the land suffices as constructive possession (qabd hukmi). The passage highlights an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf and its resolution over time.

Key Terms
روایت (riwāyah): A narrated ruling from early Hanafi authorities; here two different reports exist.
مستقرض (mustaqriḍ): The borrower; in the second narration, the land owner is considered a borrower of the seed.
قبض (qabḍ): Possession; necessary for a loan contract. Here, seed attachment to land constitutes possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied upon) position in the later Hanafi school, who gets the produce in an invalid muzara'ah contract?
A) The land owner, because the seed becomes part of his land.
B) The seed owner, by analogy to other invalid muzara'ah cases.
C) Both share it equally.
D) The worker, because he labored.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that the produce in invalid muzara'ah belongs to the seed owner, by analogy to other invalid contracts.

The Sixth Invalid Form of Muzara'ah: Combining Seed and Oxen
Ruling on a specific invalid form

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sixth invalid form of muzara'ah and explain the legal reasoning for its invalidity.

Core Idea
Combining individually corrupt elements does not cure the contract.

In the previous forms, we saw invalid contracts where seed, land, or oxen were allocated improperly. The sixth form presents a combination: one party provides both seed and oxen, the other provides land and labor. This combination is invalid because each element on its own would be corrupt, and their combination does not remove the defect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties' contributions
In this form, one party (Zayd) provides seed and oxen; the other party ('Amr) provides land and labor.
2
Recognize the individual corruption
If one party provided seed and oxen alone and the other provided land and labor alone, each of those allocations is individually invalid in muzara'ah because they mix ownership and responsibility incorrectly.
Recall earlier invalid forms.
3
Apply the accumulation principle
Combining two invalid allocations does not make the contract valid; the corruption persists.
The text says: 'it is not permissible individually, so likewise in combination.'
4
Conclude the ruling
The contract is fasid (invalid).
No valid muzara'ah can be based on this arrangement.
