Book of Muzara'ah. This is against the law. This partnership between seed and labor is not permissible because of difference in genus. Sixth form: And the second is to combine seed and oxen, and it is not permissible because it is not permissible individually, so likewise in combination. Translation: The sixth form is when Zayd's oxen and 'Amr's land and labor are combined; this is invalid. In invalid muzara'ah, to whom does the produce belong? The produce in both forms: in one narration, to the owner of the seed, by analogy with other invalid muzara'ahs; in another narration, to the owner of the land, and he becomes a borrower of the seed, taken possession by attachment to his land. Explanation: Two narrations: first, produce to seed-owner; second, produce to land-owner as borrower. Question: For loan, possession is required; here no possession. Answer: When seed attaches to land, it becomes possession. Sadr al-Shahid mentioned both narrations. I (Shami) say: In Durr al-Mukhtar, Bada'i', Majma' al-Anhur, etc., the second narration is not found; rather all books state that in invalid muzara'ah, produce belongs to the seed-owner. Then if the seed-owner is the landowner, the worker gets wages; if the worker is the seed-owner, the landowner gets land rent.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage begins by continuing the discussion of invalid forms of muzara'ah. The sixth invalid form is when one party provides seed and oxen while the other provides land and labor. This is invalid because the combination of things from different parties (seed and oxen from one side, land and labor from the other) mirrors individually invalid arrangements. The text then shifts to a general rule: in all invalid muzara'ah contracts, whose produce is it? Here, al-Hidayah presents two narrations (riwayat) from the early masters. The first narration, which is relied upon (mufta bihi), is that the produce belongs to the owner of the seed, by analogy with other invalid contracts. The second narration says the produce belongs to the landowner, who then owes the seed-owner the value of the seed as a loan. A question arises: a loan requires actual possession of the seed, but here the seed is sown. The answer is that when the seed is attached to the land, it is considered possession by the landowner. However, later authoritative books like Durr al-Mukhtar and Bada'i' confirm only the first narration. Therefore, the fatwa is that produce belongs to the seed-owner. Then, compensation is worked out: if the seed-owner is also the landowner, he pays the worker wages; if the worker owns the seed, the landowner pays him rent for the land.

Key Terms
مزارعة فاسدة (muzāra‘ah fāsidah): A sharecropping contract that is invalid due to missing a condition or presence of a corrupting element.
بذر (badhr): Seeds used for planting; ownership of seeds determines primary right to produce in invalid contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sixth invalid form of muzara'ah, what is the ruling?
A) Valid, because all parties contribute
B) Invalid, because combining corrupt elements does not remove corruption
C) Valid, if shares are known
D) Invalid, only if seed is from the worker

Key Takeaway
The sixth invalid form shows that combining two individually invalid allocations in muzara'ah does not yield a valid contract; it remains fasid.

Produce Ownership in Invalid Muzara'ah: Two Hanafi Narrations
Dispute on produce ownership in invalid muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi narrations on produce ownership in invalid muzara'ah and state the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
In invalid muzara'ah, produce belongs to the seed-owner, per the relied-upon narration.

After listing invalid forms, al-Hidayah presents a general rule for all invalid muzara'ah: whose produce is it? Two narrations exist from Imam Abu Hanifa. The first, which is established in the reliable books, assigns produce to the seed-owner. The second, reported by Sadr al-Shahid but absent in later major works, assigns it to the landowner. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the first narration
Produce belongs to the seed-owner, by analogy with other invalid muzara'ah contracts.
This is the well-known position in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
State the second narration
Produce belongs to the landowner, who is considered a borrower of the seed after it attaches to his land.
Reported by Sadr al-Shahid but not found in later authoritative works.
3
Examine the evidence
First narration relies on qiyas: all invalid muzara'ah give produce to seed-owner. Second narration relies on possession via attachment: seed becomes landowner's property through attachment, and then he repays the seed as a loan.
The second narration addresses a possible counterargument regarding possession.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
Later Hanafi scholars (Shami, Durr al-Mukhtar, Bada'i') confirm only the first narration; the second is not found in major works and is thus marjuh.
Authority_weight: zahir_riwayah.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
Produce goes to seed-owner. Then, if the seed-owner is also the landowner, the worker gets wages. If the seed-owner is the worker, the landowner gets land rent.
This is the standard compensation for invalid contracts.

Book of Muzara'ah. This is against the law. This partnership between seed and labor is not permissible because of difference in genus. Sixth form: And the second is to combine seed and oxen, and it is not permissible because it is not permissible individually, so likewise in combination. Translation: The sixth form is when Zayd's oxen and 'Amr's land and labor are combined; this is invalid. In invalid muzara'ah, to whom does the produce belong? The produce in both forms: in one narration, to the owner of the seed, by analogy with other invalid muzara'ahs; in another narration, to the owner of the land, and he becomes a borrower of the seed, taken possession by attachment to his land. Explanation: Two narrations: first, produce to seed-owner; second, produce to land-owner as borrower. Question: For loan, possession is required; here no possession. Answer: When seed attaches to land, it becomes possession. Sadr al-Shahid mentioned both narrations. I (Shami) say: In Durr al-Mukhtar, Bada'i', Majma' al-Anhur, etc., the second narration is not found; rather all books state that in invalid muzara'ah, produce belongs to the seed-owner. Then if the seed-owner is the landowner, the worker gets wages; if the worker is the seed-owner, the landowner gets land rent.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage begins by continuing the discussion of invalid forms of muzara'ah. The sixth invalid form is when one party provides seed and oxen while the other provides land and labor. This is invalid because the combination of things from different parties (seed and oxen from one side, land and labor from the other) mirrors individually invalid arrangements. The text then shifts to a general rule: in all invalid muzara'ah contracts, whose produce is it? Here, al-Hidayah presents two narrations (riwayat) from the early masters. The first narration, which is relied upon (mufta bihi), is that the produce belongs to the owner of the seed, by analogy with other invalid contracts. The second narration says the produce belongs to the landowner, who then owes the seed-owner the value of the seed as a loan. A question arises: a loan requires actual possession of the seed, but here the seed is sown. The answer is that when the seed is attached to the land, it is considered possession by the landowner. However, later authoritative books like Durr al-Mukhtar and Bada'i' confirm only the first narration. Therefore, the fatwa is that produce belongs to the seed-owner. Then, compensation is worked out: if the seed-owner is also the landowner, he pays the worker wages; if the worker owns the seed, the landowner pays him rent for the land.

Key Terms
مزارعة فاسدة (muzāra‘ah fāsidah): A sharecropping contract that is invalid due to missing a condition or presence of a corrupting element.
بذر (badhr): Seeds used for planting; ownership of seeds determines primary right to produce in invalid contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The state treasury

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position in invalid muzara'ah is that produce belongs to the seed-owner, with the other party receiving compensation for their contribution.

Conditions for Valid Muzara'ah: Fixed Term and Common Share
Ruling statement with illustrative furū'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two essential conditions for a valid muzara'ah contract and identify stipulations that invalidate it.

Core Idea
A muzara'ah contract is valid only if the term is known and the produce is shared as an undivided common share.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies two core requirements for a sharecropping contract. Without a known term or with a stipulated fixed quantity for one party, the contract becomes fasid (invalid). Understanding these conditions protects parties from entering into void agreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
From the text, find the two explicit conditions: a known term (mudda ma'luma) and that the produce be shared as a common undivided share (shā'i').
These are shurut al-sihhah (conditions of validity).
2
Understand why fixed quantity invalidates
The text says stipulating a fixed number of measures (qafīz) for one party destroys the partnership because the land might yield only that amount, leaving nothing for the other.
The key principle is shuyū' (commonality); any condition that cuts it off invalidates.
3
Analyze the analogy to mudārabah
The text compares to mudārabah where stipulating fixed dirhams invalidates. Recognize that the same principle applies: partnership requires common sharing of profit/produce.
This is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Distinguish valid from invalid furū'
The text presents two furū': invalid when seed-owner takes seed first and remainder shared; valid when seed-owner gets a fraction (e.g., one-tenth) as a common share before division.
The difference is whether the condition preserves or destroys commonality.
5
Apply the principle to new scenarios
Given any stipulation, ask: does it fix a specific quantity for one party before common division? If yes, it likely invalidates the contract.
Always check for shuyū'.

وكذا إذا شرطا ان يرفع صاحب البذر بذره ويكون الباقى بينهما نصفين لانه يؤدى الى قطع الشركة في بعض معين اوفى جميعه بان لم يخرج الا قدر البذر وصار كما اذا شرطا رفع الخراج والارض خراجية وان يكون الباقى بينهما بخلاف ما اذا شرط صاحب البذر عشر الخارج لنفسه او للآخر والباقى بينهما لانه معين مشاع فلا يؤدى الى قطع الشركة كما اذا شرطا رفع العشر وقسمة الباقى بينهما والارض عشرية
He (al-Quduri) said: Muzara'ah is not valid except for a known term, as we have explained, and that the produce be shared between them in a common (shā'i‘) manner, to realize the meaning of partnership. If they stipulate for one of them a specified number of measures (qafīz), it is invalid because thereby the partnership is cut off, since the land may not yield more than that amount, and it becomes like stipulating counted dirhams for one of them in partnership (mudārabah). Translation: Al-Quduri said: Muzara'ah is not valid except for a known term and that the produce be common between them. If they stipulate specified measures for one, it is invalid because partnership is cut off. Explanation: The eight conditions for valid muzara'ah were mentioned before. Now two further points are mentioned. Point 1: Without specifying the term, muzara'ah is invalid. Since muzara'ah is a form of partnership, any condition that destroys partnership is invalid. The requirement is that produce be common (shā'i‘). If they stipulate that one party takes a fixed amount first and the rest is shared, then commonality is not achieved, so the contract is fasid. Similarly, every condition that destroys commonality is invalid. And likewise if they stipulate that the seed-owner takes back his seed and the remainder is shared half-half, because it cuts off partnership in a specific part or in all if only the seed amount is produced. This is different from stipulating that the seed-owner gets one-tenth of the produce for himself or the other, and the rest is shared, because that is a specified common share (mu‘ayyan shā‘i‘) and does not cut off partnership, like stipulating the deduction of 'ushr (tithe) and dividing the remainder, when the land is 'ushriyya.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage deals with two essential conditions for a valid muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract: a known duration (mudda ma'luma) and that the produce be shared as a common undivided share (shā'i‘) between the parties. The text quotes al-Quduri's matn and then provides commentary. The first condition: the term must be clearly specified, otherwise the contract is invalid. The second condition: the share of each party must be a fraction of the total produce (like half, one-third), not a fixed quantity. If they stipulate for one party a fixed number of measures (e.g., 10 qafīz), the contract is invalid because it destroys the partnership: the land might yield exactly that amount, leaving nothing for the other. This is analogous to mudārabah where stipulating a fixed profit amount invalidates the contract. The commentary then gives two illustrative furū‘ (branches). First: if they stipulate that the seed-owner takes back his seed first and then the remainder is divided, this is invalid because it cuts off partnership in a part. However, if they stipulate that the seed-owner gets a fraction (like one-tenth) of the total produce for himself, and the rest is shared, that is valid because it is a common share (mu‘ayyan shā‘i‘). This is analogous to deducting the 'ushr (tithe) from the produce before division when the land is 'ushriyya (subject to tithe). The key principle: any condition that eliminates commonality (shuyū‘) in the produce invalidates the contract.

Key Terms
شائع (shā‘i‘): An undivided common share in the produce, not a fixed quantity.
قفزان (qafīzān): A fixed measure of grain (e.g., a specific number of qafeez).
مضاربة (muḍārabah): A profit-sharing partnership where one provides capital and the other labor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following stipulations would make a muzara'ah contract invalid?
A) The term is one agricultural season.
B) The produce is divided equally.
C) The worker gets 50 qafīz of wheat before any further division.
D) The landowner provides seeds.

Key Takeaway
A valid muzara'ah requires a known term and an undivided common share; any condition that cuts off commonality invalidates the contract.

The Condition of Shuyu' in Muzara'ah: Valid and Invalid Stipulations
Explains the requirement of common proportional share and examples of invalid and valid stipulations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish valid from invalid stipulations in a muzara'ah contract by applying the condition of shuyu' (common proportional share) and explain the Hanafi reasoning.

Core Idea
Fixed allocations break the partnership; only proportional shares preserve the validity of muzara'ah.

In sharecropping (muzara'ah), the produce must be shared as a common proportion between landowner and worker to reflect the partnership. This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar walks through several stipulations – some invalid because they fix a quantity or allocate a specific area, and one valid (the 'ushr) because it remains proportional. Understanding this distinction is key to structuring valid agricultural partnerships in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
State the two essential conditions for a valid muzara'ah contract: a specified duration and that the produce be shared as a common proportional share (shuyu').
This is the foundation for evaluating all stipulations.
2
Analyze the First Invalid Stipulation
Consider the stipulation where one party gets a fixed measure (qafiz) of grain. Explain why it severs the partnership, using the analogy to mudarabah.
Fixed quantity creates a risk of only that amount being produced, leaving nothing for the other party.
3
Analyze the Second Invalid Stipulation
Consider the stipulation where the seed owner first takes back his seed in kind, then divides the remainder. Show how this can cut the partnership partially or completely.
Analogous to deducting kharaj before division – both are invalid if they allocate a prior fixed portion.
4
Analyze the Valid Stipulation
Consider the stipulation where one party gets the 'ushr (tenth) of the entire produce first, then the remainder is divided proportionally. Explain why this preserves shuyu'.
The 'ushr is a fraction of the whole, so the partnership remains common.
5
Analyze Invalid Spatial Allocations
Consider stipulations that assign specific areas (e.g., along canals, or one side to one party). Show how these break shuyu' because they allocate a defined portion of the land's produce.
The partnership requires undivided common shares; spatial division contradicts that.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا تصح المزارعة الا على مدة معلومة لما بينا وان يكون الخارج شائعا بينهما تحقيقا لمعنى الشركة فان شرطا لاحدهما قفزانا مسماة باطلة لان به تنقطع الشركة لان الأرض عساها لا تخرج الا هذا القدر وصار كاشتراط دراهم معدودة لاحدهما في المضاربة
وكذا إذا شرطا ان يرفع صاحب البذر بذره ويكون الباقى بينهما نصفين لانه يؤدى الى قطع الشركة في بعض معين اوفى جميعه بان لم يخرج الا قدر البذر وصار كما اذا شرطا رفع الخراج والارض خراجية وان يكون الباقى بينهما بخلاف ما اذا شرط صاحب البذر عشر الخارج لنفسه او للآخر والباقى بينهما لانه معين مشاع فلا يؤدى الى قطع الشركة كما اذا شرطا رفع العشر وقسمة الباقى بينهما والارض عشرية
قال و کذالک ان شرطا ما على الماذيانات والسواقى معناه لاحدهما لانه اذا شرط لاحدهما زرع موضع معین افضی ذالک الى قطع الشركة لانه لعله لا يخرج الا من ذالك الموضع وعلى هذا اذا شرط لاحدهما ما يخرج من ناحية معينة ولآخر ما يخرج من ناحية اخرى
He (al-Quduri) said: Muzara'ah is not valid except for a specified period, for the reason we have stated, and that the produce be common between them in a proportional manner to realize the meaning of partnership. So if they stipulate for one of them specified measures (qafiz), it is invalid because thereby the partnership is severed, for the land may not produce except that amount, and it becomes like stipulating a fixed number of dirhams for one of them in mudarabah. Likewise, if they stipulate that the owner of the seed take his seed and the rest be half between them, because it leads to cutting the partnership in a specific part or in all of it, if nothing comes out except the amount of the seed, and it becomes like when they stipulate the removal of the kharaj when the land is kharaji, and the rest between them. Unlike when the owner of the seed stipulates the 'ushr (tenth) of the produce for himself or for the other, and the rest between them, because it is a specified but proportional share and does not lead to cutting the partnership, just as when they stipulate the removal of the 'ushr and division of the rest between them when the land is 'ushri. He said: And likewise if they stipulate what is on the irrigation channels and water courses, meaning for one of them, because if they stipulate for one of them the crop of a specific place, that leads to cutting the partnership, because it may not come out except from that place. And according to this, if they stipulate for one of them what comes out from a specific side and for the other what comes out from another side.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Muzara'ah (Book of Sharecropping) discusses the crucial condition of shuyu' (common proportional share) for the validity of a muzara'ah contract. The author, al-Quduri, states the general rule: the produce must be shared as a common proportion between the owner and the worker, reflecting the partnership nature. Any stipulation that allocates a fixed quantity (like specific qafiz) to one party is invalid because it severs the partnership—the land might yield only that amount, leaving nothing for the other. This is analogous to mudarabah where a fixed number of dirhams cannot be stipulated for one party. Similarly, if the seed owner stipulates that he first takes back his seed (in kind) and then divides the remainder, it is invalid. This could cut the partnership either partially (if the produce exceeds the seed) or completely (if the produce equals the seed). The same applies if they stipulate to deduct the kharaj (land tax) first from the produce before division. However, if they stipulate that one party gets the 'ushr (one-tenth) of the entire produce first, and then the remainder is divided proportionally, it is valid. This is because the 'ushr is a proportional share (musha') of the entire produce, so the partnership is preserved. This is analogous to 'ushri land where the tithe is deducted first. Finally, stipulating that one party gets the crop from specific areas (like along irrigation channels) is invalid, as it allocates a defined portion of the land's produce, potentially cutting the partnership if only that area yields.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzara'ah): A sharecropping contract where one party provides land and the other works it, with produce shared according to agreement.
شائع (shai'): Commonly shared in a proportional, undivided manner (musha').
قفزانا مسماه (qafizāna musammā): Stipulated fixed measures of grain (qafiz) for one party.
عشر ('ushr): One-tenth of the produce, a proportional share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following stipulations in a muzara'ah contract is valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) The landowner gets 10 qafiz first, then the rest is divided equally.
B) The worker gets all the produce from the eastern side of the field, and the landowner gets from the western side.
C) The seed owner takes back his seed (in kind) first, then the remainder is divided equally.
D) The worker gets one-tenth of the entire produce, and the remainder is divided equally.

Key Takeaway
A muzara'ah contract is only valid if the produce is shared as a common proportional share (shuyu'); any fixed or spatial allocation invalidates the stipulation.

Fixed Amount Condition Invalidates Muzara'ah
Ruling with rational proof: condition of fixed amount invalidates muzara'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why a condition to take a fixed amount of produce before division invalidates a muzara'ah contract and apply the principle to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
A fixed amount condition in muzara'ah destroys shuyu' and makes the contract fasid.

Muzara'ah (sharecropping) is a partnership in produce, not a fixed return. The Hanafi school holds that any condition that eliminates proportional sharing (shuyu') invalidates the contract. This passage illustrates that rule with concrete examples, including an analogy with kharaj taxation. Understanding this principle prevents unintended contract nullification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key legal act
Recognize that the passage deals with muzara'ah (sharecropping). The core issue: a condition that one party takes a fixed amount of produce before dividing the remainder.
Muzara'ah is a partnership; the produce must be shared proportionally.
2
State the Hanafi principle
The Hanafi school requires shuyu' (proportional sharing) in all partnership contracts, including muzara'ah. Any condition that destroys shuyu' renders the contract fasid (invalid).
Shuyu' means the produce is owned in common until division.
3
Apply the principle to the fixed amount condition
If one party stipulates, 'I will first take my capital (or a fixed amount) and then share the remainder,' this eliminates shuyu' because it allocates a specific portion to one party before division. This is corrupting regardless of whether the produce exceeds the fixed amount or not.
The condition is invalid in all outcomes: partial or total elimination of shuyu'.
4
Analyze the analogy with kharaj
The text compares the condition to deducting kharaj (land tax) before sharing the produce. In a kharaji land, if they agree to first deduct the fixed tax and then divide the rest, it also invalidates the contract because it removes a specific part from the common pool.
In 'ushri land, if they similarly deduct 'ushr and share the remainder, it is valid because 'ushr is a proportional share (musha') and does not eliminate partnership.
5
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, any condition that specifies a fixed amount for one party before division is a corrupting condition (shart mufsid). The contract becomes fasid, meaning it must be rescinded or corrected.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جبکہ دونوں نے شرط کی ہو خراج کے اٹھانے کی حالانکہ زمین خراجی ہو اور یہ کہ ہوگا باقی ان دونوں کے درمیان بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ بیچ والے نے اپنے لئے پیداوار کے عشر کی شرط لگائی ہو یا دوسرے کیلئے اور باقی ان دونوں کے درمیان اس لئے کہ یہ معین مشاع ہے تو یہ شرکت کو ختم کرنے کی جانب مودی نہ ہو گا ۔ جیسے کہ دونوں نے عشر کے اٹھانے کی شرط کی ہو اور باقی کو اپنے درمیان تقسیم کرنے کی حالانکہ زمین عشری ہے۔ تشریح ہر وہ شرط جو شیوع کو ختم کر دے مفید مزارعت ہوگی تو بیچ والے نے کہا کہ میں پہلے پیداوار میں سے اپنے پیج کی مقدار لوں گا پھر باقی دونوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا تقسیم کیا جائے گا تو یہ شرط مفسد مزارعت ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر پیداوار پیج سے زیادہ ہوگئی تو بقدر پیج شرکت ختم ہوئی جو مفسد ہے اور اگر بیچ سے زیادہ پیداوار نہ ہو شرکت بالکل ختم ہوگئی اور یہ بھی مفسد ہے۔ اور یہ بالکل ایسا ہے کہ یہ زمین خراجی ہو جس کا سالانہ مثلاً دس من غلہ مقرر ہے۔ اب ان دونوں نے عقد مزارعت کیا کہ پہلے خراج کی مقدار پیداوار سے نکال لیں گے پھر باقی کو آدھا آدھا تقسیم کریں گے تو یہ جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ بعض معین یا کل میں شرکت ختم ہو گئی۔ بعینہ یہی صورت پہلی شرط میں ہے۔
And this becomes like when both stipulated the removal of kharaj while the land is kharaji, and the remainder between them, unlike the case when one of them stipulated the 'ushr of the produce for himself or for the other, and the remainder between them, because this is a specific musha', so it does not lead to cutting off partnership. Just as if both stipulated the removal of 'ushr and dividing the remainder between themselves while the land is 'ushri. Explanation: Every condition that eliminates shuyu' nullifies muzara'ah. So if one said, 'I will first take the amount of my capital from the produce, then the remainder will be divided half and half between us,' this condition is a corrupting condition. Because if the produce exceeds the capital, partnership is eliminated to the extent of the capital, which is corrupting; and if produce does not exceed the capital, partnership is completely eliminated, which is also corrupting. And this is exactly like the land being kharaji with an annual fixed amount, e.g., ten man of grain. They make a muzara'ah contract that first the amount of kharaj is taken from the produce, then the remainder is divided half and half. This is not permissible, because partnership is eliminated in a specific part or in entirety. Exactly this is the case in the first condition.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with rational proof. It explains that any condition in a muzara'ah contract that specifies a fixed amount of produce for one party before division invalidates the contract. The reason is that such a condition eliminates the required partnership (shirkah) in the produce. The commentator gives an analogy: if the land is kharaji (subject to a fixed tax), and they agree to first deduct the tax and then share the remainder, it is invalid because the fixed amount removes partnership. Similarly, if one party takes a fixed capital amount first, it is invalid. The core principle is that shuyu' (proportional sharing) must be maintained throughout the produce.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzara'ah): Sharecropping contract between landowner and worker
شرط (shart): Condition stipulated in the contract
شيوع (shuyu'): Proportional sharing or common ownership
خراج (kharaj): Fixed land tax on kharaji land
عشر ('ushr): Tithe, a fixed proportion (10%) of produce

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the amount is unknown
B) Because it eliminates the proportional partnership (shuyu')
C) Because it is a form of gambling
D) Because it benefits one party more

Key Takeaway
A condition to take a fixed amount of produce before division in muzara'ah eliminates the required proportional partnership (shuyu') and renders the contract fasid.

Condition of Specific Location Invalidates Muzara'ah
Ruling with proof explaining why location-specific conditions invalidate muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why stipulating produce from a specific location in a muzara'ah contract renders it invalid and apply the same reasoning to analogous conditions.

Core Idea
Specifying a location for produce in muzara'ah destroys partnership and invalidates the contract.

Muzara'ah is a partnership in cultivation where both parties share the entire produce proportionally. When one party tries to secure a specific part of the harvest (e.g., from near channels or a corner), it undermines the joint ownership required by the contract. This lesson explores why such conditions are invalid and the reasoning behind the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and contract
Recognize that the condition assigns all produce from a specific physical location to one party, while the other party gets the rest or a different location.
Examples: 'produce near channels is mine' or 'produce from the eastern corner is mine'.
2
Understand the ruling
The contract of muzara'ah becomes invalid (batil) due to this condition.
The ruling is explicit in the text.
3
Grasp the legal reasoning (dalil aqli)
The condition may lead to one party receiving nothing if only the specified location yields produce, thus cutting off the required partnership in the entire produce.
Al-Quduri explains: 'perhaps nothing is produced except from that place'.
4
Check analogical application
The same ruling applies if each party is assigned a different direction or corner.
The text says: 'upon this, if he stipulates for one of them what comes out of a specific direction...'
5
Conclude the ruling
Any condition that segregates produce by location destroys partnership, so the contract is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہر ایک نے یہ شرط لگائی کہ جو پیداوار نالیوں کے آس پاس ہوگی وہ میری ہوگی یا کھیت کے متعین کونہ کی پیداوار میری ہوگی ان صورتوں میں مزارعت باطل ہے.
قال و کذالک ان شرطا ما على الماذيانات والسواقى معناه لاحدهما لانه اذا شرط لاحدهما زرع موضع معین افضی ذالک الى قطع الشركة لانه لعله لا يخرج الا من ذالك الموضع وعلى هذا اذا شرط لاحدهما ما يخرج من ناحية معينة ولآخر ما يخرج من ناحية اخرى
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور ایسے ہی ( مزارعت باطل ہے ) اگر انہوں نے شرط کی ہو اس پیداوار کی جو نالیوں پر ہوتی ہے یعنی ان دونوں میں سے ایک کیلئے اسلئے کہ جب ان دونوں میں سے ایک کیلئے معین جگہ کی کھیتی کی شرط کی گئی ہو تو یہ قطع شرکت کی جانب مفضی ہوگا اس لئے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ زمین سے اس جگہ کے علاوہ سے پیدا نہ ہو اور اسی طریقہ پر جبکہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کیلئے وہ پیداوار شرط ہو جو کسی معین و نہ سے پیدا ہو اور دوسرے کیلئے وہ جو دوسرے گوشہ سے پیدا ہو۔
تشریح اگر ایک نے یہ شرط لگائی کہ جو پیداوار نالیوں کے آس پاس ہوگی وہ میری باقی دوسری کی یا کھیت کے اس کونہ کی پیداوار میری اور دوسرے کو نہ کی دوسرے کی تو یہ شرطیں شرکت کو ختم کر دینے والی ہیں اسلئے ان صورتوں میں مزارعت باطل ہوگی ۔ ماذیانات۔ اور سواقی نالیاں، گویا دونوں مترادف الفاظ ہیں۔ وفيه اقوال آخر
Each one stipulated that the produce near the channels will be mine, or the produce of a specific corner of the field will be mine; in these cases, muzara'ah is invalid.
He (al-Quduri) said: And similarly (muzara'ah is invalid) if they stipulate what is on the drains and channels, meaning for one of them, because if he stipulates for one of them the cultivation of a specific place, this leads to cutting off partnership, because perhaps nothing is produced except from that place. And upon this, if he stipulates for one of them what comes out of a specific direction and for the other what comes out of another direction.
Translation: Al-Quduri said: And similarly (muzara'ah is invalid) if they stipulate the produce that is on the channels, meaning for one of them, because when they stipulate for one of them a specific place of cultivation, this leads to cutting off partnership, because perhaps nothing is produced except from that place. And in the same way, when for one of them the produce that comes out of a specific corner is stipulated and for the other that which comes out of another corner.
Explanation: If one stipulated that the produce near the channels will be mine, the rest for the other, or the produce of this corner for me and the other for the other, these conditions eliminate partnership, so in these cases muzara'ah is invalid. 'Madhiyanat' and 'Sawaqi' are channels, both are synonyms. And there are other sayings (on this).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, quoting Quduri. It states that if a condition assigns produce from a specific physical location (e.g., near channels or a specific corner) to one party, the contract becomes invalid. The reasoning is that such a condition may lead to one party getting nothing if only that location produces, thus eliminating the required partnership. The same applies if each party is assigned a specific direction. The explanation clarifies that the Arabic terms 'madhiyanat' and 'sawaqi' both refer to channels or drains. The phrase 'wa fihi aqwal ukhar' indicates there are other opinions, likely referring to further discussions.

Key Terms
ماذيانات (madhiyanat): Drains or channels for irrigation
سواقي (sawaqi): Irrigation channels

Key Takeaway
Any condition in muzara'ah that allocates produce by specific location invalidates the contract because it destroys the required partnership in the entire yield.

Condition Allocating Grain and Straw Separately Invalidates Muzara'ah
Ruling with rational proof from Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that allocating grain to one party and straw to the other in a muzara'ah contract makes the contract fasid, and explain the rational proof based on the risk of total loss.

Core Idea
Allocating grain to one and straw to other destroys partnership and risks total loss.

This lesson examines a specific condition in sharecropping: dividing the primary crop (grain) and its byproduct (straw) between the parties. The Hanafi school rules such a condition invalid because it eliminates the required partnership in the main produce and introduces unacceptable uncertainty (gharar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional stipulation
Recognize that the contract specifies one party gets the grain and the other gets the straw.
2
Distinguish primary and secondary produce
Grain is the main objective of the contract; straw is a byproduct.
3
Apply the rationale of disaster risk
If a calamity destroys the grain, the party entitled to grain receives nothing while the other still gets straw. This breaks the necessary partnership in the primary produce.
4
Conclude with the ruling
Because the condition eliminates partnership and creates uncertainty, the contract becomes fasid (invalid).
5
Acknowledge the Hanafi position
This is the relied-upon view from Zahir al-Riwayah. Other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک کیلئے غلہ دوسرے کیلئے بھوسہ کی شرط لگائی تو بھی مزارعت فاسد ہے.
وكذا اذا شرط لا حدهما التبن وللاخر الحب لانه عسى يصيبه افة فلا ينعقد الحب ولا يخرج الا التبن
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی جب ان میں سے ایک کیلئے بھوسہ کی شرط ہو اور دوسرے کیلئے غلہ کی اسلئے کہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ اس کو کوئی آفت پہنچ جائے پس دانہ نہ پڑ سکے اور بھوسہ کے علاوہ کچھ نہ نکلے۔
تشریح اگر یہ شرط ہوئی کہ ایک کو غلہ اور دوسرے کو بھوسہ ملے گا تو چونکہ شرکت ندارد ہے اسلئے مزارعت فاسد ہے اور اس کی وجہ ظاہر ہے۔
If a condition is made for one grain and for the other straw, then also muzara'ah is invalid.
And similarly if he stipulates straw for one of them and grain for the other, because perhaps a calamity will befall it, so the grain will not form and only straw will come out.
Translation: And similarly when for one of them straw is stipulated and for the other grain, because it is possible that a calamity befalls it, so the grain does not set and nothing comes out except straw.
Explanation: If this condition is made that one gets grain and the other straw, since there is no partnership, therefore muzara'ah is invalid, and its reason is obvious.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Quduri. It states that if the contract allocates grain to one party and straw to the other, it is invalid. The reason given is the risk of calamity: if a disaster prevents grain formation, the party entitled to grain gets nothing while the other gets straw, destroying the necessary partnership in the produce. The commentator notes that the absence of partnership (shirkah) in the primary produce (grain) makes the contract invalid.

Key Terms

تبن (tibn): Straw, the byproduct

Key Takeaway

Invalid Condition in Muzara'ah: Straw Shared but Grain Exclusively for One
States that sharing straw equally but giving all grain to one is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when straw is shared equally but grain is given entirely to one party in a muzara'ah contract, and explain the rationale based on partnership in the main produce.

Core Idea
A muzara'ah contract is invalid if partnership in the main produce (grain) is absent, even if the byproduct (straw) is shared.

In sharecropping (muzara'ah), the core purpose is sharing the crop. The Hanafi school strictly requires partnership in the primary produce—grain. Even if parties agree to share straw equally, allocating all grain to one party destroys the essential partnership, rendering the contract invalid (fasid). This lesson unpacks that ruling and its rational basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the stipulated condition
Read the condition: straw is shared half and half, but grain is exclusively for one party. Note that both elements (straw and grain) are part of the produce.
2
Assess partnership in the primary objective
Determine whether the condition creates partnership in the main objective of muzara'ah. Grain (habb) is the primary objective; straw (tibn) is secondary.
The Hanafi school considers the main crop as the intended benefit.
3
Apply the Hanafi ruling
Since there is no partnership in grain, the condition cuts off the essential element of the contract. Therefore, the contract is fasid (invalid).
Fasid means the contract is void in its basis; it does not produce legal effects.
4
State the rationale (dalil aqli)
The rationale is that muzara'ah is built on sharing the produce; grain is the main produce. Without partnership in grain, the contract loses its purpose. This is a rational proof (qiyas) based on the nature of the contract.
The proof is derived from the objectives of the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بھوسہ دونوں کیلئے نصف نصف اور غلہ ایک ک توسی شرط کی وجہ مزارعت فاسد ہے.
وكذا اذا شرط التبن نصفين والحب لا حدهما بعينه لانه يؤدى الى قطع الشركة فيما هو المقصود وهو الحب
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی (باطل ہے مزارعت ) جبکہ بھوسہ کی شرط کی گئی ہو آدھے آدھے کی اور دانہ معین کر کے ان میں سے ایک کیلئے اس لئے کہ یہ شرکت کے ختم کرنے کی جانب مودی ہو گا اس چیز میں جو کہ مقصود ہے اور وہ دانہ ہے۔
تشریح اگر دونوں نے یہ شرط کی کہ بھوسہ آدھا آدھا اور غلہ ان میں سے ایک کا تو یہ شرط فاسد ہے جو عقد کو فاسد کر دے گی کیونکہ اصل مقصود غلہ ہے نہ کہ بھوسہ اور غلہ میں شرکت نہیں ہے۔
If straw is stipulated half and half for both, and grain exclusively for one, then muzara'ah is invalid.
And similarly if he stipulates straw in halves and grain specifically for one of them, because it leads to cutting off partnership in what is intended, which is grain.
Translation: And similarly (muzara'ah is invalid) when straw is stipulated half and half and grain specifically for one of them, because it leads to eliminating partnership in that which is intended, and that is grain.
Explanation: If both stipulated that straw is half and half and grain for one of them, this condition is fasid, which will make the contract fasid, because the main objective is grain, not straw, and there is no partnership in grain.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. Even if straw is shared equally, if grain is allocated entirely to one party, the contract is invalid. The reason is that grain is the primary objective of muzara'ah; partnership in grain is essential. Sharing only the byproduct (straw) does not fulfill the required partnership in the main produce. The commentator emphasizes that the absence of partnership in grain is the cause of invalidity.

Key Terms
حَبّ (habb): Grain, the main crop
تبن (tibn): Straw, byproduct

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a condition of sharing straw equally but giving all grain to one party invalid in a muzara'ah contract?
A) Because straw is worthless
B) Because partnership in grain, the main objective, is absent
C) Because the parties did not agree
D) Because straw must also be shared

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi muzara'ah, partnership must exist in the primary produce (grain); a condition that excludes grain partnership invalidates the contract.

Straw Ownership in Silent Muzara'ah Contracts
Rules on straw distribution in a silent muzara'ah contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the main Hanafi position on straw ownership in a silent muzara'ah contract and explain the alternative view of the Mashayikh of Balkh.

Core Idea
Silence on straw does not invalidate the contract; straw belongs to the seed owner unless custom dictates otherwise.

In this passage, we examine a common scenario in muzara'ah (sharecropping) where the partners stipulate equal division of grain but forget to mention straw. Is the contract valid? And who gets the straw? The text presents the mainstream Hanafi ruling and contrasts it with a differing opinion from the Mashayikh of Balkh, highlighting how custom ('urf) can influence subsidiary matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its terms
Determine what type of contract is being discussed, what is stipulated (grain shared equally), and what is omitted (straw).
The contract is muzara'ah (sharecropping).
2
Determine the validity of the contract
Assess whether the contract is valid despite the omission. Note that partnership in the main objective (grain) is present.
The text says the contract is valid (صحت).
3
Apply the main Hanafi ruling on straw
Identify the owner of the seed and explain why straw goes to that party according to the main view.
Straw is growth of seed owner's property.
4
Analyze the alternative view from Balkh
Explain the reasoning of the Mashayikh of Balkh: they rely on custom ('urf) and the principle that straw is a follower (tabi') of grain.
The follower follows the condition of the origin.
5
Contrast the two positions and identify the practical difference
Compare the outcomes: seed owner gets all straw vs. straw shared. Consider the role of custom in the Balkh view.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear.

غلہ نصف نصف اور بھوسہ کا تذکرہ نہیں کیا تو مزارعت درست ہے.
ولو شرطا الحب نصفين ولم يتعرضا للتبن صحت لاشتراطهما الشركة فيما هو المقصود ثم التبن يكون لصاحب البذر لانه نماء ملكه وفى حقه لا يحتاج الى الشرط والمفسد هو الشرط وهذا سكوت عنه وقال مشائخ بلخ رحهم الله التبن بينهما ايضا اعتباراً للعرف فيما لم ينص عليه المتعاقد ان ولانه تبع للحب والتبع يقوم بشرط الاصل
ترجمہ اور اگر ان دونوں نے شرط کی دانے کی آدھا آدھا اور بھوسہ سے کچھ تعرض نہیں کیا تو مزارعت بھی ہے ان دونوں کے شرط کرنے کی وجہ سے شرکت کی اس چیز میں جو کہ مقصود ہے پھر بھوسہ بیج والے کا ہو گا اسلئے کہ وہ اس کی ملک کی بہ ھو تہ نا ہے اور اس کے حق میں شرط کی حاجت نہیں ہے اور فاسد کرنے والی وہ شرط ہے اور یہ اس سے (بھوسہ سے ) سکوت ہے اور مشائخ بلیچ نے فرمایا کہ بھوسہ بھی ان دونوں کے درمیان ہوگا عرف کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اس چیز میں جس پر عاقدین نے صراحت نہیں کی اور اسلئے کہ بھوسہ دانہ کے تابع ہے اور تابع قائم ہوتا ہے اصل کی شرط کے مطابق۔
If grain is stipulated half and half and straw is not mentioned, then muzara'ah is valid.
And if they stipulate grain in halves and do not mention straw, it is valid due to their stipulation of partnership in what is intended. Then straw belongs to the owner of the seed, because it is growth of his property, and in his right he does not need a condition, and the corrupting element is the condition, and this is silence about it. And the Mashayikh of Balkh (may Allah have mercy on them) said that straw is also between them, considering custom in what the contracting parties did not specify, and because straw is a follower of grain, and the follower stands on the condition of the origin.

Then straw will belong to the owner of the seed, because it is the growth of his property, and in his right there is no need for a condition; the corrupting element is the condition, and this is silence regarding it. And the Mashayikh of Balkh said that straw is also between them, taking custom into account in that which the contracting parties did not specify, and because straw is a follower of grain, and the follower is established by the condition of the origin.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a intra-Hanafi dispute. It states that if the contract specifies grain to be shared equally but is silent on straw, the contract is valid because partnership in the main objective (grain) exists. Then it presents the main Hanafi position: straw belongs solely to the owner of the seed, since it is a growth of his property and no condition was made to share it. However, the Mashayikh of Balkh hold that straw should be shared between both parties, relying on custom (urf) and the principle that the follower (straw) is subject to the condition of the origin (grain). This is a difference within the Hanafi school: the main position from the matn says straw is for the seed owner, while the later scholars from Balkh opine that it is shared based on custom and tab'iyyah.

Key Terms
بذر (badhr): Seed; in muzara'ah, the party providing seed
تبع (tabi'): Follower; something subsidiary to the main
عرف ('urf): Customary practice

Muzara'ah Void if Grain and Straw Are Allocated to Separate Parties
Ruling on conditional allocation of grain and straw in muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when one party is allocated grain and the other straw in muzara'ah, and explain why the contract is fasid.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah requires partnership in the main produce; allocating grain to one and straw to the other destroys that partnership.

In this lesson, we examine a specific condition that invalidates a muzara'ah contract: stipulating that one party receives the grain (the main crop) and the other receives only the straw (the byproduct). The Hanafi school rules such a condition voids the entire contract because it prevents true partnership in the primary produce. We will explore the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind this ruling and its practical implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition Stated
Read the stipulation: one party gets the grain (habb) and the other gets the straw (tibn). Recognize that this allocates the two outputs of the crop to different parties separately.
2
State the Legal Ruling
The text explicitly says the muzara'ah is fasid (void). Confirm that this is the position of the Hanafi school as stated in Al-Hidayah.
3
Analyze the Proof Given (Ta'lil)
The author provides a hypothetical: a crop failure could occur, so only straw is produced and no grain. In that case, the party entitled to grain receives nothing, while the other gets straw. This shows the condition destroys the necessary partnership in the main produce.
The proof is a rational analysis (qiyas/talil) that the condition is inherently destructive to partnership.
4
Link to the Principle of Partnership
Muzara'ah is a contract of partnership (shirkah) in the produce. The primary produce is the grain; straw is a secondary byproduct. The condition allocates these different outputs to different parties, halting the required co-ownership of the grain. Hence, the contract is void.

Source Text

ایک کیلئے غلہ دوسرے کیلئے بھوسہ کی شرط لگائی تو بھی مزارعت فاسد ہے كتاب المزارعة وكذا اذا شرط لا حدهما التبن وللاخر الحب لانه عسى يصيبه افة فلا ينعقد الحب ولا يخرج الا التبن ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی جب ان میں سے ایک کیلئے بھوسہ کی شرط ہو اور دوسرے کیلئے غلہ کی اسلئے کہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ اس کو کوئی آفت پہنچ جائے پس دانہ نہ پڑ سکے اور بھوسہ کے علاوہ کچھ نہ نکلے۔ تشریح اگر یہ شرط ہوئی کہ ایک کو غلہ اور دوسرے کو بھوسہ ملے گا تو چونکہ شرکت ندارد ہے اسلئے مزارعت فاسد ہے اور اس کی وجہ ظاہر ہے۔
And similarly, when condition is made for one of them the straw and for the other the grain, because it is possible that an affliction may befall it, so the grain may not form and nothing but straw is produced. Commentary: If this condition is made that one will get grain and the other straw, then since partnership is absent, the muzara'ah is void, and its reason is apparent.

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: if the contracting parties stipulate that one party will receive the grain (the main produce) and the other will receive only the straw (the byproduct), the muzara'ah contract is void (fasid). The proof given is that it is possible a crop failure occurs, so only straw is produced, and the party entitled to grain gets nothing, while the other gets straw. This condition eliminates the required partnership in the primary yield (grain), which is the essence of muzara'ah. Therefore, the contract becomes void due to the absence of partnership in the main produce.

Key Terms

تبن (tibn): Straw, the byproduct of grain after threshing.

Key Takeaway

The Essential Role of Grain Partnership in Muzara'ah
Ruling on a condition excluding grain from partnership in muzara'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why sharing only straw but excluding grain from partnership invalidates a muzara'ah contract, and apply the ruling to similar stipulations.

Core Idea
In muzara'ah, partnership in the main crop (grain) is essential; excluding it invalidates the contract.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific stipulation in a sharecropping contract: the parties agree to share straw equally but give all grain to one party. The contract is ruled fasid (void) because it destroys the very partnership that defines muzara'ah. Understanding this ruling requires recognizing the primary objective of muzara'ah – the grain harvest – and the condition's effect on it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Identify the contract: muzara'ah with a condition (straw half-half, grain for one). State the ruling: the contract is fasid (void).
The ruling applies regardless of the parties' consent.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is qiyas: the condition 'يؤدي إلى قطع الشركة فيما هو المقصود وهو الحب' (it leads to cutting off partnership in the intended objective, which is grain).
The proof is based on the nature of muzara'ah as a partnership.
3
Trace the legal reasoning (talil)
Why does excluding grain invalidate? Because muzara'ah is a shirkah (partnership) in the produce, and the primary product is grain; straw is secondary. Excluding grain severs the core partnership.
The illa (cause) is the absence of partnership in the main crop.
4
Note the consequence
The condition is fasid, and because it is integral to the contract, the entire contract becomes fasid.
A fasid contract can be rectified by removing the invalid condition before execution.
5
Consider intra-Hanafi agreement
All three main Hanafi authorities (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on this ruling; there is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The ruling is zaahir al-riwaayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بھوسہ دونوں کیلئے نصف نصف اور غلہ ایک کیلئے شرط کی وجہ مزارعت فاسد ہے وكذا اذا شرط التبن نصفين والحب لا حدهما بعينه لانه يؤدى الى قطع الشركة فيما هو المقصود وهو الحب ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی (باطل ہے مزارعت) جبکہ بھوسہ کی شرط کی گئی ہو آدھے آدھے کی اور دانہ معین کر کے ان میں سے ایک کیلئے اس لئے کہ یہ شرکت کے ختم کرنے کی جانب مودی ہو گا اس چیز میں جو کہ مقصود ہے اور وہ دانہ ہے۔ تشریح اگر دونوں نے یہ شرط کی کہ بھوسہ آدھا آدھا اور غلہ ان میں سے ایک کا تو یہ شرط فاسد ہے جو عقد کو فاسد کر دے گی کیونکہ اصل مقصود غلہ ہے نہ کہ بھوسہ اور غلہ میں شرکت نہیں ہے۔
And similarly, when straw is stipulated in halves and grain for one of them specifically, because it leads to cutting off partnership in that which is the intended objective, which is grain. Commentary: If both stipulate that straw is half-half and grain for one of them, then this condition is void and renders the contract void, because the real objective is grain, not straw, and there is no partnership in grain.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage rules that if the parties agree that straw will be shared equally (half-half) but grain belongs entirely to one of them, the contract is void (fasid). The proof: this condition cuts off partnership in the main objective (grain). Since the essence of muzara'ah is partnership in the produce, and grain is the primary product, allocating grain exclusively to one party destroys the partnership. Straw is secondary; the main output is grain. Therefore, any stipulation that removes grain from partnership invalidates the contract.

Key Terms
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership; in muzara'ah, it refers to the sharing of produce between the parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Void because partnership in grain is absent.
C) Valid if both agree.
D) Void only if crop fails.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi muzara'ah, partnership in the primary crop (grain) is essential; a condition that excludes it renders the contract void (fasid).

Two Opinions on Straw Distribution in Muzara'ah
Two Hanafi opinions on straw distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi opinions on straw ownership in a valid muzara'ah contract and explain the legal basis for each (nama' mulkihi vs. 'urf and taba'iyyah).

Core Idea
When straw is not mentioned, the seed owner claims it as his property's increase, but custom may make it shared.

In a valid muzara'ah contract where grain is shared half-half but straw is not mentioned, a dispute arises over straw ownership. This lesson presents two opinions within the Hanafi school: one assigns all straw to the seed owner based on property increase, the other divides it equally based on custom and the principle that the follower (straw) takes the ruling of the principal (grain). Understanding this dispute helps appreciate how Hanafi jurists balance textual principles with customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the missing term
Note that the parties stipulated grain in halves but remained silent about straw. The contract is valid because the main objective (grain) is covered.
Silence (sukut) on straw does not invalidate the contract; it is only problematic if a condition contradicts the contract's essence.
2
State the first opinion and its rationale
The main position: straw belongs to the seed owner because it is the natural increase (nama') of his property. He does not need a stipulation; the invalidation comes from a harmful condition, not from silence.
This relies on the principle that one's property is entitled to its growth without explicit condition.
3
State the second opinion and its rationale
The scholars of Balkh hold that straw is shared between the parties. Their reasoning: custom ('urf) in such contracts, and straw is a follower (tabi') of grain; the follower follows the ruling of the original, so since grain is shared, straw is also shared.
This opinion invokes the Hanafi recognition of 'urf and the legal maxim al-tabi' tabi'.
4
Contrast the legal principles
Compare ownership through property increase (nama' mulkihi) vs. customary sharing and taba'iyyah. The first focuses on individual ownership, the second on equity and common practice.
No textual dalil is cited; both rely on general legal reasoning (talil) and school consensus.
5
Identify the practical consequence
Under the first opinion, the seed owner takes all straw; under the second, both parties share it equally. The text does not resolve which is mufta bihi, leaving both as valid positions.
In practice, later Hanafi texts may lean toward custom, but the dispute remains a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلہ نصف نصف اور بھوسہ کا تذکرہ نہیں کیا تو مزارعت درست ہے ولو شرطا الحب نصفين ولم يتعرضا للتبن صحت لاشتراطهما الشركة فيما هو المقصود ثم التبن يكون لصاحب البذر لانه نماء ملكه وفى حقه لا يحتاج الى الشرط والمفسد هو الشرط وهذا سكوت عنه وقال مشائخ بلخ رحهم الله التبن بينهما ايضا اعتباراً للعرف فيما لم ينص عليه المتعاقد ان ولانه تبع للحب والتبع يقوم بشرط الاصل ترجمہ اور اگر ان دونوں نے شرط کی دانے کی آدھا آدھا اور بھوسہ سے کچھ تعرض نہیں کیا تو مزارعت بھی ہے ان دونوں کے شرط کرنے کی وجہ سے شرکت کی اس چیز میں جو کہ مقصود ہے پھر بھوسہ بیج والے کا ہو گا اسلئے کہ وہ اس کی ملک کی بہ ھو تہ نا ہے اور اس کے حق میں شرط کی حاجت نہیں ہے اور فاسد کرنے والی وہ شرط ہے اور یہ اس سے (بھوسہ سے ) سکوت ہے اور مشائخ بلیچ نے فرمایا کہ بھوسہ بھی ان دونوں کے درمیان ہوگا عرف کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اس چیز میں جس پر عاقدین نے صراحت نہیں کی اور اسلئے کہ بھوسہ دانہ کے تابع ہے اور تابع قائم ہوتا ہے اصل کی شرط کے مطابق۔  تشریح عاقدین نے غلہ کے دونوں کے درمیان مشترک ہونے کی شرط کر لی اور بھوسہ کا کوئی ذکر نہیں آیا تو چونکہ اصل مقصود وہ غلہ ہے اور اسمیں شرکت ہے لہذا مزارعت صحیح ہوگی۔ اب یہ سوال ہوگا کہ بھوسہ کس کو ملے تو فرمایا کہ اس میں دو قول ہیں۔ -1 بیج والے کو کیوں کہ یہ اس کی ملک کی بڑھوتری ہے کما ہو ظاہر ۔ -۲- عرف کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے بھوسہ بھی مشترک ہوگا اور چونکہ دانہ اصل اور بھوسہ تابع ہے اور تابع کا وہی حکم ہوتا ہے جو اصل کا ہوتا ہے لہذا کھوسہ بھی مشترک ہو گا۔ وفى حقه لا يحتاج .... الخ ۔ یعنی بیج والے کے حق میں بھوسہ کے ثبوت کیلئے شرط کی حاجت نہیں اور جن صورتوں میں مزارعت فاسد ہوتی ہے وہ شرط کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے اور یہاں تو سرے سے شرط ہی نہیں بلکہ سکوت ہے اور سکوت مفسد نہیں ہے وہ دوسری بات ہے کہ یہاں اگر شرط بھی ہوتی جب بھی فسادنہ ہوتا۔ ( کما سیاتی)
And if both stipulated grain in halves and did not mention straw, it is valid because they stipulated partnership in what is intended; then the straw belongs to the owner of the seed because it is the growth of his property, and in his right there is no need for a stipulation, and the invalidator is the condition, and this is silence about it. The scholars of Balkh said: the straw is also between them, considering custom in what the contractors did not specify, and because it is a follower of grain, and the follower stands on the condition of the original. Commentary: The contractors stipulated grain as common, and straw was not mentioned; so the contract is valid. There are two opinions: First: to the seed owner because it is the increase of his property. Second: considering custom, straw is also shared; grain is the original, straw is the follower, so it follows the ruling of the original.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the distribution of straw when it is not mentioned in the muzara'ah contract. The contract is valid because the parties have stipulated partnership in grain (the main objective). However, there are two opinions on who gets the straw: (1) The seed owner gets it, because straw is a natural increase of his property (the seed). (2) The scholars of Balkh hold that straw is shared between the parties, based on custom ('urf) and because straw is a follower (tabi') of grain; since grain is shared, its follower (straw) should also be shared. The text notes that silence (sukut) about straw does not invalidate the contract; it only becomes problematic if a condition is stipulated that contradicts the contract's requirements.

Key Terms
تابع (tābi‘): Follower; something that follows the ruling of its original (asl).
عرف (‘urf): Custom or common practice among people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because straw is the seed owner's property.
B) Because straw is a follower of grain, which is shared.
C) Because both parties agreed to share everything.
D) Because the contract is void otherwise.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two valid opinions on straw distribution in a silent muzara'ah contract: one gives all to the seed owner, the other shares it equally based on custom and the principle of taba'iyyah.

Stipulating Straw for Seed Owner in Muzara'ah
Ruling on stipulating straw for seed owner in valid muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stipulating straw for the seed owner in muzara'ah and explain its validity using the concept of hukm al-'aqd.

Core Idea
Stipulating straw for seed owner is valid because it confirms the contract's default ruling.

In sharecropping (muzara'ah), the default distribution of produce is critical. Hanafi fiqh establishes that straw belongs to the seed owner by default. This lesson examines a case where the parties explicitly stipulate this distribution, and we see why such a condition does not invalidate the contract but rather aligns with its inherent ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sub-cases
The passage presents two scenarios: one where straw is given to the seed owner (valid) and one where it is given to someone else (invalid). Distinguish them.
2
Isolate the valid condition
Focus on the valid case: grain half-half, straw for seed owner. Note the explicit condition.
3
Understand the proof 'hukm al-'aqd'
The condition is valid because it matches the contract's default ruling (hukm al-‘aqd). Default: straw belongs to seed owner. Thus, the condition does not contradict the contract's essence.
Match this with the dalil: 'li-annahu hukm al-‘aqd'.
4
Contrast with the invalid condition
If straw is stipulated for the other party (e.g., the worker), it contradicts the default, cutting off partnership, rendering the contract fasid (voidable).
5
Apply the principle
Any condition that contradicts the contract's inherent ruling invalidates it; any condition that confirms it is valid. Recognize this pattern for future cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غله نصف نصف اور بھوسہ کی بیج والے کیلئے شرط لگائی تو مزارعت درست ہے ولو شرط الحب نصفين والتبن لصاحب البذر صحت لانه حكم العقد وان شرطا التين للاخر فسدت لانه شرط يؤدى الى قطع الشركة بان لا يخرج الا التبن واستحقاق غير صاحب البذر بالشرط ترجمہ اور اگر دونوں نے دانہ کی شرط آدھے آدھے کی کی اور بھوسہ کی بیج والے کیلئے تو مزارعت صحیح نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ یہ عقد کا حکم اور اگر ان دونوں نے بھوسہ کی شرط دوسرے ( بیج والے کے غیر کیلئے ) تو مزارعت فاسد ہوگی اسلئے کہ یہ ایسی شرط ہے جو قطع شرکت کی جانب پہنچائے گی اس طریقہ پر کہ بھوسہ کے علاوہ نہ پیدا ہو سکے اور بیج والے کے غیر کا استحقاق شرط کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح یعنی اگر یہ طے ہو گیا کہ غلہ مشترک اور بھوسہ بیج والے کا تو چونکہ یہ شرط مقتضاء عقد کے خلاف نہیں بلکہ عین مطابق ہے اسلئے یہ مزارعت درست ہے۔
And if they stipulate grain in halves and straw for the owner of the seed, it is valid because it is the ruling of the contract. But if they stipulate straw for the other, it is void because it is a condition that leads to cutting off partnership, such that only straw may be produced, and the entitlement of someone other than the seed owner is by condition. Commentary: If they decided that grain is common and straw for the seed owner, this condition is not contrary to the requirement of the contract but rather precisely in accordance with it, so the muzara'ah is valid.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage addresses two sub-cases. First, if the parties stipulate that grain is shared half-half and straw belongs to the seed owner, the contract is valid. The reason is that this stipulation aligns with the default ruling (hukm al-'aqd) of the contract: straw already goes to the seed owner by default when not stipulated, as seen earlier. Therefore, explicitly stating it does not violate the contract's requirements. The condition is consistent with the contract's essence.

Key Terms
حكم العقد (hukm al-‘aqd): The inherent ruling or default consequence of the contract; here, straw belongs to seed owner by default.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is stipulating straw for the seed owner considered valid in muzara'ah?
A) Because it matches the contract's default ruling.
B) Because the seed owner is the landowner.
C) Because both parties agreed.
D) Because straw is worthless.

Key Takeaway
A condition that merely confirms the contract's default ruling is valid; one that contradicts it invalidates the contract.

Muzara'ah Void if Straw Specified for Non-Seed Owner
Ruling on stipulating straw for the party other than seed owner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stipulating straw for the non-seed owner in muzara'ah and explain why the condition is invalid.

Core Idea
A condition that severs partnership invalidates muzara'ah, even if both parties agree.

In muzara'ah (sharecropping), the seed owner is inherently entitled to the straw. If the parties stipulate that straw goes to the other party, this condition contradicts the contract's default requirement. This lesson explains why such a condition renders the contract void (fasid).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the hukm (legal classification) of the contract when straw is stipulated for the non-seed owner.
The text says 'fasid' (void).
2
Understand the default entitlement
Recall that the seed owner is entitled to straw without any condition (bilā sharṭ). This is the muqtada al-aqd (contractual requirement).
Muqtada al-aqd: what the contract inherently implies.
3
Analyze the condition
The condition giving straw to the other party only benefits that party through a stipulation, which runs contrary to the default.
4
Apply the rationale
The condition cuts off partnership in a possible scenario – if only straw is produced, the seed owner gets nothing. This destroys the partnership (qat' al-shirkah), which is essential in muzara'ah.
Cutting partnership is a mufsid (invalidating factor) for muzara'ah.
5
Conclude the ruling
Since the condition is invalid and contradicts the contract's nature, the entire contract becomes fasid.
Fasid means defective; the contract is not valid as agreed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر بھوسہ کی شرط دوسرے کیلئے لگائی تو اب مزارعت فاسد ہوگی کیونکہ شہر طاعقد کے تقاضہ کے خلاف ہے۔ او استحقاق ... الخ - یعنی بی والا کھوسہ کا مستحق ہو جائے تو بلاشرط بھی ہو سکتا ہے کمامر ۔ اور دوسرا بھوسہ کا مستحق صرف شرط کی وجہ سے ہو سکتا ہے اور چونکہ یہ شرط مقتضاء عقد کے خلاف ہے اسلئے کہ شرط فاسد ہے کیونکہ اس سے شرکت ختم ہو جاتی ہے او قطع شرکت مفسد مزار بخت ہے۔
And if they stipulate straw for the other (non-seed owner), then the muzara'ah becomes void because it is contrary to the requirement of the contract. The seed owner is entitled to straw without condition, as mentioned; the other can only get straw by condition. Since this condition is contrary to the contract's requirement, the condition is void, because it ends partnership, and cutting partnership invalidates muzara'ah.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage completes the previous ruling. If the parties stipulate that straw belongs to the worker or the other party (not the seed owner), the condition is invalid and renders the contract void (fasid). The reason: the seed owner is already entitled to straw by default (without condition). Giving straw to the other party requires a condition that contradicts the contract's inherent ruling (muqtada al-'aqd). Moreover, such a condition cuts off partnership entirely if, hypothetically, only straw is produced, then the seed owner gets nothing while the other gets straw. This destroys the partnership, which is essential in muzara'ah.

Key Terms
مقتضى العقد (muqtaḍā al-‘aqd): The requirement or intrinsic dictate of the contract; what the contract inherently implies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid because both agreed.
B) Void because the condition cuts off partnership in the main produce.
C) Valid only if the worker also gets a share of grain.
D) Void only if the crop fails.

Key Takeaway
Stipulating straw for the non-seed owner renders muzara'ah fasid because it contradicts muqtada al-aqd and severs the required partnership.

Distribution of Produce in Valid Muzara'ah
General rule on produce distribution in valid muzara'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the distribution rule in a valid muzara'ah, explain the consequence of no produce, and distinguish it from ijarah and void contracts.

Core Idea
In valid muzara'ah, the worker has no claim unless produce exists.

Muzara'ah is a partnership in cultivation where the landowner provides land and the worker provides labor. In a valid contract, the produce is shared exactly as stipulated. The worker's entitlement is tied to the actual output; if nothing grows, he receives nothing. This contrasts with ijarah (lease) where a fixed wage is due regardless, and with void contracts where an equivalent wage becomes a debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage concerns a valid muzara'ah contract. The ruling is that produce is distributed according to the condition (shart) agreed upon.
The condition must be lawful and clearly stated.
2
Understand the consequence of no produce
If the land yields nothing, the worker gets nothing. This is because his right is through partnership in the produce; nonexistent produce cannot be shared.
The worker bears the risk of crop failure.
3
Contrast with ijarah (lease)
In ijarah, the worker (or lessee) is entitled to a fixed named wage (ujr musamma) regardless of output. This distinguishes muzara'ah from a pure service contract.
The named wage is a debt in ijarah, not a share of produce.
4
Contrast with void (fasid) muzara'ah
In a void muzara'ah, the worker is entitled to ujr al-mithl (equivalent wage) as a liability in the dhimmah. This remains due even if no produce results.
Ujr al-mithl is determined by market rates for similar work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مزارعت صحیح ہونے کی صورت میں پیداوار شرط کے مطابق تقسیم ہوگی قال و اذا صحت المزارعة فالخارج على الشرط لصحة الالتزام و ان لم تخرج الارض شيئاً فلا شيء للعامل لانه يستحقه شركةً ولا شركة فى غير الخارج و ان كانت اجارة فالاجر مسمى فلا يستحق غيره بخلاف ما اذا فسدت لان اجر المثل في الذمة ولا تفوت الذمة بعدم الخارج
When the muzara'ah is valid, the produce is on the condition (stipulated). If the land produces nothing, the worker gets nothing because he deserves it through partnership, and there is no partnership in non-existent produce. If it were a lease (ijarah), the named hire would be due, and he would not deserve anything else. Contrary to when it is void, because the equivalent hire is a liability in the dhimmah, and the dhimmah does not cease due to non-existence of produce.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental principle in muzara'ah: In a valid contract, the produce is distributed exactly as agreed upon (shart). The worker only gets a share from the actual output; if nothing grows, he gets nothing because his entitlement is through partnership in the produce. This differs from ijarah (lease), where the worker (lessee) is entitled to a fixed wage regardless of output. In a void (fasid) muzara'ah, the worker gets the equivalent wage (ujr al-mithl), which remains a debt in the worker's liability (dhimmah) even if no produce results.

Key Terms
اجرت مثل (ujr al-mithl): Equivalent wage; the market rate for similar work in a void contract.
الخارج على الشرط (al-kharij 'ala al-shart): The produce is according to the condition; distribution follows the agreed-upon share.
شركة (shirkah): Partnership; in muzara'ah, the worker's entitlement is through partnership in the produce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a valid muzara'ah, if the land yields nothing, what does the worker receive?
A) A fixed wage.
B) Nothing, because his share is from actual produce.
C) half of the straw.
D) The equivalent wage.

Key Takeaway
In valid muzara'ah, the worker's share is conditional on the existence of produce; if none, he gets nothing.

Stipulating Straw in Muzara'ah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on straw ownership in muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi opinions on default straw ownership and apply the rule that stipulating straw for the seed owner is valid while for the other party invalidates the contract.

Core Idea
Straw ownership in muzara'ah: silence does not invalidate, but condition for the non-seed owner cuts partnership.

In a sharecropping (muzara'ah) contract, the primary concern is the grain, but what about the straw? The Hanafi school presents two opinions when no condition is mentioned. Additionally, the ruling differs sharply depending on which party is allocated the straw by stipulation. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind these positions and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule when straw is not stipulated
The contract is valid because the primary object (grain) is shared. But two opinions exist: straw belongs to seed owner as increase of his property, or it is shared by custom since it is subsidiary to grain.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Distinguish stipulation for seed owner vs. other
If they stipulate grain half-half and straw for seed owner, it is valid because it aligns with the contract's inherent ruling (hukm al-aqd). If they stipulate straw for the other party, it is invalid because it cuts off partnership.
The condition for the other party is seen as contrary to the contract's nature.
3
Analyze the rationale for invalidity of the second stipulation
The condition could lead to a situation where only straw is produced, and the non-seed owner would be entitled to it only by a condition that is void (fasid) because it ends the partnership.
Cutting off partnership (qat' al-shirkah) is a recognized cause of invalidity in muzara'ah.
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If no condition is mentioned, one opinion gives all straw to seed owner; the other shares it. This directly affects distribution in silent contracts.
The text does not prefer one default opinion; both remain within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المزارعة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ تشریح عاقدین نے غلہ کے دونوں کے درمیان مشترک ہونے کی شرط کر لی اور بھوسہ کا کوئی ذکر نہیں آیا تو چونکہ اصل مقصود وہ غلہ ہے اور اسمیں شرکت ہے لہذا مزارعت صحیح ہوگی۔
اب یہ سوال ہوگا کہ بھوسہ کس کو ملے تو فرمایا کہ اس میں دو قول ہیں۔
